4️⃣ Unified Remeasurement Model (Locked Rule)

Across all engines:

No in-place mutation

Supersession is new-row-only

Schedule regeneration always version-token-based

Journals reference only effective version

Supersession chains validated (no cycles, no branching)

Event ordering deterministic:

event_date ASC

engine-specific precedence rules

created_at ASC

id ASC

Replay is now idempotent and stable.

5️⃣ FX Policy (Locked)

Selected-rate service only

No raw provider table access in engines

Default:

Revenue/Lease → daily (legacy)

Prepaid/FAR → month_end_locked

Month-end locked mode fails closed

Missing lock throws MISSING_LOCKED_RATE

FX fields persisted on financially impacting rows

6dp rate quantization

2dp output

6️⃣ Supersession Rules (Locked)

Self-referential supersedes_id

Linear chain only

No branching

No cycles

Effective version resolution deterministic

Version tokens hashed deterministically

No row mutation

7️⃣ Journal Lineage Rule (Locked)

Each journal row must reference exactly one source:

depreciation row OR

impairment row OR

disposal row OR

schedule row OR

revenue allocation row OR

lease liability row

Never:

multiple sources

zero sources

Drill path must always resolve:
journal → schedule/event → asset/contract → source artifact

Terminal completion requires lineage completeness.

Good. We now move to Phase 1F.1 — MIS Manager audit-grade design.

This phase is not about pretty dashboards. It is about building the layer that can understand uploaded MIS files, learn structure safely, version that structure, detect gaps, and regenerate outputs deterministically.

What 1F.1 must achieve
The MIS Manager should do five things well:

Ingest uploaded files

Detect structure

Convert that structure into a canonical template

Version and freeze that template

Load periodic data against that template with validations

So the idea is simple:

First upload = learn the pattern

Next uploads = validate against the learned pattern

If format changes = detect drift, do not silently accept

If mapping breaks = fail clearly

If usable = produce normalized MIS data for reconciliation, ratios, and board pack feeds

1. Boundary rule first
This is the most important rule.

MIS Manager is not allowed to:
change accounting engine tables directly

regenerate revenue / lease / prepaid / FAR schedules

bypass control plane or RLS

write journals

mutate prior template versions

silently re-map changed columns

MIS Manager is allowed to:
ingest uploaded files

infer file structure

create append-only template versions

map columns / sections to canonical metrics and dimensions

store normalized snapshots

raise exceptions / gaps / drift alerts

expose deterministic extracts for later layers

This keeps your accounting core clean.

2. Recommended module structure
Use a separate module family, not mixed into engine code.

Suggested package tree
backend/src/modules/mis_manager/
  domain/
    entities.py
    enums.py
    value_objects.py
  application/
    ingest_service.py
    template_detection_service.py
    mapping_service.py
    snapshot_service.py
    drift_detection_service.py
    validation_service.py
  infrastructure/
    repository.py
    file_parser_excel.py
    file_parser_csv.py
  api/
    routes.py
    schemas.py
  policies/
    control_plane_policy.py
  tests/
    unit/
    integration/
Reason:

detection logic stays separate

mapping logic stays separate

snapshot persistence stays separate

future AI-assisted interpretation can be added without touching deterministic core

3. Core domain objects
You need to think in template, version, mapping, snapshot, exception.

3.1 Template
Represents the overall MIS design for a tenant / org / use case.

Example:

Monthly P&L MIS

BU profitability MIS

Project performance MIS

Consolidated management pack

3.2 Template Version
Represents a frozen version of the detected layout and mapping logic.

If row structure changes, this should become a new version, not an overwrite.

3.3 Mapping
Explains how input columns / sections / row bands map into canonical measures and dimensions.

Example:

“Net Revenue” row → canonical_metric = revenue_net

“Cost of Delivery” → cogs_service

“Department” column → dimension = cost_center

3.4 Snapshot
Represents one uploaded reporting period interpreted using a specific template version.

Example:

Jan 2026 MIS upload

Feb 2026 MIS upload

3.5 Exception / Drift
Represents gaps like:

expected row missing

new unknown column

time column shifted

section moved

formula row changed

duplicate key combinations

Do not let every client MIS remain custom forever.

6. Detection pipeline
This should be deterministic.

Step 1 — File intake
accept xlsx / csv initially

compute source hash

store upload artifact

record tenant / org / user / period intent

Step 2 — Sheet profiling
For each sheet:

used range

header candidates

blank row density

merged cells presence

likely data block ranges

formula density

text vs numeric ratio

Step 3 — Structure detection
Identify:

header row

data start row

section breaks

subtotal rows

period columns

dimension columns

notes columns

Step 4 — Signature generation
Create deterministic signatures:

header signature

row label signature

section signature

column order signature

Step 5 — Template match
Compare with existing effective template versions.

Outcome:

exact match

match with tolerable drift

no match → candidate new template version

Step 6 — Mapping resolution
Map:

source columns → canonical dimensions / roles

row labels → canonical metrics

subtotal patterns → section hierarchy

Step 7 — Validation
Check:

required metrics present

required periods present

numeric consistency

duplicate dimensional grain

subtotal sanity

sign consistency

Step 8 — Snapshot creation
Create immutable snapshot and normalized lines.

7. Drift handling policy
This must be strict.

Minor drift examples
header wording changed slightly

one optional note column added

column moved but identifiable

cosmetic blank row inserted

These may be auto-accepted if confidence is high.

Major drift examples
metric rows renamed materially

new section inserted

period axis changed

pivot structure changed

dimensions changed

totals logic changed

These must:

create drift event

fail closed or hold in review

not silently load into existing template

That is the audit-safe approach.

8. Control plane requirements
Since Phase 1E is already active, MIS Manager must obey the same control model.

Every ingestion must require:

valid context token

tenant routing

module enabled = mis_manager

RBAC permission

quota availability

organisation scoping

Suggested permissions:

mis_template_create

mis_template_review

mis_snapshot_upload

mis_snapshot_approve

mis_snapshot_view

mis_exception_resolve

Do not allow broad generic access.

9. Append-only rules for MIS module
Carry forward your platform doctrine.

Locked rules for MIS:
no overwrite of template versions

no overwrite of normalized snapshots

no silent reclassification of prior snapshots

no mutation of mapping history

all exceptions append-only

all drift decisions append-only

effective template resolution deterministic

This matters because later someone will ask:
“Why did February output differ from January?”

You need an exact answer:

different template version

different snapshot

different mapping approval

different source artifact

10. Validation rules to build first
Start with hard rules, not AI guessing.

Must-have validations
one reporting period or period set detected

at least one measurable numeric block

required revenue / expense anchor rows for P&L templates

duplicate row+dimension combinations blocked

subtotal rows identified and excluded from base grain unless explicitly mapped

formulas allowed, but stored as values + formula metadata if present

mixed currency within one snapshot flagged unless supported explicitly

hidden sheets ignored unless configuration says otherwise

11. API surface — first cut
Keep this small and clean.

Suggested endpoints
Template intake
POST /mis/templates/detect

POST /mis/templates/commit-version

Snapshot intake
POST /mis/snapshots/upload

POST /mis/snapshots/{id}/validate

POST /mis/snapshots/{id}/finalize

Review / drift
GET /mis/templates

GET /mis/templates/{id}/versions

GET /mis/snapshots/{id}

GET /mis/snapshots/{id}/exceptions

GET /mis/drift-events/{id}

Extracts
GET /mis/snapshots/{id}/normalized-lines

GET /mis/snapshots/{id}/summary

Do not overbuild APIs in phase 1.

12. Deterministic processing rules
This is a big one.

When the same file is uploaded again under the same template/version/rules, output should be identical.

So:

hash source file

hash chosen sheet

hash selected structure

hash mapping set

hash validation rule set

produce snapshot token deterministically

That gives you replayability.

13. AI usage boundary
You do want intelligence here, but not uncontrolled behavior.

AI can help with:
probable header identification

likely row label matching

semantic similarity of line item names

proposed mappings

confidence scores

AI must not:
directly commit template versions

override deterministic rule failures

silently alter historical mapping

bypass validation

write final normalized data without deterministic approval path

So AI is assistant, not authority.

That is the right governance model.

We are continuing from a post-Phase 1D.6 harmonized accounting engine state.

Phase 1F.1 — MIS Manager (Audit-Grade Design + Schema + Implementation Skeleton)

This module sits ABOVE accounting engines.

It must not:

Mutate engine tables

Create journals

Regenerate schedules

Bypass control plane

Violate append-only principles

🎯 OBJECTIVE
Design and implement a deterministic, append-only MIS ingestion and template management system that:

Learns structure from uploaded Excel/CSV files

Detects template structure deterministically

Versions templates append-only

Detects layout drift

Stores normalized snapshots

Exposes deterministic extracts

Obeys control-plane isolation

Preserves replay stability

🔒 ARCHITECTURAL INVARIANTS (MANDATORY)
The MIS Manager must obey:

Append-only tables only

No update-in-place for template versions

Linear supersession chain for template versions

Deterministic version_token hashing

Deterministic snapshot_token hashing

No mutation of historical snapshots

No silent drift acceptance

All ingestion failures must be explicit

All exceptions append-only

Control-plane enforcement required for every API

RLS ENABLE + FORCE on all new tables

All writes go through AuditWriter

Idempotent re-upload behavior

Deterministic structure detection (no randomness)

AI suggestions cannot auto-commit structural changes

Phase 1f1 Mis Manager Audit Grade Master Prompt

🔐 MASTER IMPLEMENTATION PROMPT
Phase 1F.1 — MIS Manager (Audit‑Grade Design, Fully Expanded, No Omissions)
SYSTEM CONTEXT
We are continuing from a post‑Phase 1D.6 harmonized accounting engine state.

The platform already has:

Deterministic accounting engines: Revenue, Lease, Prepaid, Fixed Assets

Version‑token based forward regeneration

Append‑only DB discipline

Linear supersession chains

Journal one‑of lineage enforcement

FX month‑end fail‑closed policy where applicable

RLS ENABLE + FORCE

Control‑plane enforced execution

AuditWriter‑only write path

Stable replay semantics

The accounting engine family is frozen and MUST NOT be modified in this phase.

We are now implementing:

Phase 1F.1 — MIS Manager (Audit‑Grade Design + Deterministic Schema + Canonical MIS Layer + Implementation Skeleton)

This module sits above the accounting engines.

It must NOT:

Mutate accounting engine tables

Create journals

Regenerate revenue / lease / prepaid / fixed_assets schedules

Inject FX logic into MIS workflows

Bypass control plane or RLS

Violate append‑only principles

Silently remap changed input layouts

It IS allowed to:

Ingest files

Detect structure

Create append‑only template versions

Create append‑only snapshots

Produce canonical normalized MIS lines

Raise drift events and ingestion exceptions

Expose deterministic extract endpoints for later reconciliation / reporting / board pack layers

🎯 OBJECTIVE
Design and implement a deterministic, append‑only MIS ingestion and template management system that:

Learns structure from uploaded Excel/CSV files

Detects template structure deterministically

Creates append‑only template versions

Detects layout drift explicitly

Stores normalized period snapshots

Preserves deterministic replay

Enforces control‑plane governance and tenant isolation

Produces canonical extractable MIS lines for downstream reconciliation, ratio, and reporting layers

🔒 ARCHITECTURAL INVARIANTS (MANDATORY)
The MIS Manager MUST obey all of the following:

Append‑only tables only

No update‑in‑place for template versions

No update‑in‑place for normalized snapshots

Linear supersession chains only

Deterministic version_token hashing

Deterministic snapshot_token hashing

No mutation of historical mapping state

No silent drift acceptance

All ingestion failures must be explicit

All exceptions append‑only

All drift decisions append‑only

Control‑plane enforcement required for every API

RLS ENABLE + FORCE on all new tables

AuditWriter‑only write path

Idempotent re‑upload behavior for identical artifacts

Deterministic structure detection (no randomness)

AI suggestions may propose mappings but cannot auto‑commit structural changes

No direct writes from MIS Manager to accounting engine tables

No journal creation logic in MIS Manager

Historical output must remain explainable by template_version + snapshot + source artifact + mapping state

🧱 BOUNDARY RULES (LOCK THESE)
MIS Manager is NOT allowed to:
Change accounting engine tables directly

Regenerate revenue / lease / prepaid / FAR schedules

Bypass control plane or tenant routing

Write journals

Mutate prior template versions

Mutate prior snapshots

Silently remap changed columns / rows

Introduce engine contamination

MIS Manager IS allowed to:
Ingest uploaded files

Infer file structure

Create append‑only template versions

Map columns / sections / row bands to canonical measures and dimensions

Store normalized snapshots

Raise exceptions / gaps / drift alerts

Expose deterministic extracts for later layers

This boundary must be reflected in code structure, service responsibilities, tests, and design docs.

🏗 MODULE STRUCTURE TO GENERATE
Create a separate module family and do NOT mix with accounting engine code.

backend/src/modules/mis_manager/

    entities.py
    enums.py
    value_objects.py
    invariants.py

Reasoning:

Detection logic must remain separate from mapping logic

Mapping logic must remain separate from snapshot persistence

Drift logic must remain separate from validation logic

Future AI‑assisted interpretation can be added without touching deterministic core behavior

🗄 FULLY EXPANDED DATABASE SCHEMA
All tables must:

Include tenant_id (NOT NULL)

Include created_at (NOT NULL DEFAULT now())

Include created_by (NOT NULL)

Enforce RLS ENABLE + FORCE

Be append‑only

Be isolated from accounting engine schemas

Have explicit indexes for deterministic lookup paths

1. mis_templates
Logical parent record for a recurring MIS design.

Columns:

id (UUID PK)

tenant_id (UUID NOT NULL)

organisation_id (UUID NOT NULL)

template_code (TEXT NOT NULL)

template_name (TEXT NOT NULL)

template_type (TEXT NOT NULL)

description (TEXT NULL)

status (TEXT NOT NULL DEFAULT 'active')

created_at (TIMESTAMP NOT NULL DEFAULT now())

created_by (UUID NOT NULL)

Constraints:

UNIQUE (tenant_id, template_code)

status check constraint limited to allowed values

Example template_type values:

pnl_monthly

balance_sheet_monthly

cashflow_monthly

department_mis

project_mis

custom

2. mis_template_versions
Append‑only frozen structure versions.

Columns:

id (UUID PK)

tenant_id (UUID NOT NULL)

template_id (UUID NOT NULL FK mis_templates(id))

version_no (INTEGER NOT NULL)

version_token (TEXT NOT NULL)

based_on_version_id (UUID NULL FK mis_template_versions(id))

supersedes_id (UUID NULL FK mis_template_versions(id))

structure_hash (TEXT NOT NULL)

header_hash (TEXT NOT NULL)

row_signature_hash (TEXT NOT NULL)

column_signature_hash (TEXT NOT NULL)

detection_summary_json (JSONB NOT NULL)

drift_reason (TEXT NULL)

status (TEXT NOT NULL DEFAULT 'candidate')

effective_from (DATE NULL)

created_at (TIMESTAMP NOT NULL DEFAULT now())

created_by (UUID NOT NULL)

Constraints:

UNIQUE (template_id, version_no)

UNIQUE (template_id, version_token)

status values limited to candidate / active / superseded / rejected

Only one active version per template

supersession chain must be linear only

No cycles allowed

No branching allowed

Required trigger logic:

Reject self‑supersession

Reject superseding across different templates

Reject multiple children pointing to same parent where that would branch effective chain

Reject cycles via recursive check

3. mis_template_sections
Logical sectioning inside a template version.

Columns:

id (UUID PK)

tenant_id (UUID NOT NULL)

template_version_id (UUID NOT NULL FK mis_template_versions(id))

section_code (TEXT NOT NULL)

section_name (TEXT NOT NULL)

section_order (INTEGER NOT NULL)

start_row_signature (TEXT NOT NULL)

end_row_signature (TEXT NOT NULL)

created_at (TIMESTAMP NOT NULL DEFAULT now())

created_by (UUID NOT NULL)

Example sections:

revenue

direct_cost

gross_margin

sga

ebitda

working_capital

Constraints:

UNIQUE (template_version_id, section_code)

UNIQUE (template_version_id, section_order)

4. mis_template_columns
Column structure metadata for each template version.

Columns:

id (UUID PK)

tenant_id (UUID NOT NULL)

template_version_id (UUID NOT NULL FK mis_template_versions(id))

source_column_label (TEXT NOT NULL)

normalized_column_label (TEXT NOT NULL)

column_role (TEXT NOT NULL)

data_type (TEXT NOT NULL)

ordinal_position (INTEGER NOT NULL)

canonical_dimension_code (TEXT NULL)

canonical_metric_code (TEXT NULL)

is_required (BOOLEAN NOT NULL DEFAULT FALSE)

is_period_column (BOOLEAN NOT NULL DEFAULT FALSE)

is_value_column (BOOLEAN NOT NULL DEFAULT FALSE)

created_at (TIMESTAMP NOT NULL DEFAULT now())

created_by (UUID NOT NULL)

column_role examples:

period

metric_name

value

dimension

subtotal_flag

formula_flag

notes

Constraints:

UNIQUE (template_version_id, ordinal_position)

role/data_type validation checks

5. mis_template_row_mappings
Row pattern mapping to canonical metrics.

Columns:

tenant_id (UUID NOT NULL)

aggregation_rule (TEXT NOT NULL)

Purpose:

Support row‑driven MIS layouts

Preserve deterministic mapping state

Constraints:

confidence_score between 0 and 1

section_code must correspond to a valid section for that template version

6. mis_data_snapshots
One append‑only record per uploaded reporting period and interpreted structure.

Columns:

created_at (TIMESTAMP NOT NULL DEFAULT now())

UNIQUE (template_version_id, snapshot_token)

snapshot_status values limited to pending / validated / finalized / failed

Purpose:

This becomes the normalized MIS layer used later by reconciliation / ratios / reporting

Constraints:

UNIQUE (snapshot_id, line_no)

validation_status limited to allowed values

severity and resolution_status check constraints

created_by (UUID NOT NULL)

Drift types may include:

HEADER_CHANGE

SECTION_REORDER

PERIOD_AXIS_CHANGE

DIMENSION_CHANGE

ROW_PATTERN_CHANGE

MAJOR_LAYOUT_CHANGE

Constraints:

Below is the Phase 1F.1 DB-backed closure pack.

This is the gate before 1F.2.

Phase 1F.1 — DB-Backed Closure Objective
Prove that MIS Manager is not only well-designed, but also:

migration-safe

Postgres-safe

RLS-safe

append-only-safe

deterministic under real DB conditions

1. Closure Status Definition
Phase 1F.1 can be marked DB-closed only if all of the following are true:

Migration 0012_phase1f1_mis_manager.py applies cleanly on a fresh Postgres database

Migration is compatible with current model definitions

All MIS tables have RLS ENABLE and FORCE

All intended append-only tables reject illegal mutation paths

Supersession trigger logic works in real DB

Snapshot idempotency is proven against Postgres

Cross-tenant access is denied in real DB

API layer enforces control-plane checks in integration tests

No accounting engine tables are modified directly or indirectly

Integration test suite passes in a live Postgres-backed environment

2. Exact Postgres Integration Verification Checklist
A. Environment Bring-up
Verify first:

Postgres reachable on intended host/port

test DB created cleanly

app test config points to correct DB

migrations table consistent

no stale schema from earlier failed runs

Checklist:

 Postgres starts successfully

 connection string resolved correctly

 test user has required privileges

 target schema is clean or recreated

 alembic/migration runner sees current head correctly

B. Migration Verification
Run migration 0012_phase1f1_mis_manager.py on fresh DB.

Check:

 migration applies without SQL errors

 all MIS tables are created

 FKs compile correctly

 unique constraints compile correctly

 partial unique index for active template version works

 triggers compile correctly

 RLS policy SQL applies successfully

 indexes are created successfully

 downgrade path is either intentionally blocked/documented or works safely

Inspect specifically:

 mis_templates

 mis_template_versions

 mis_template_sections

 mis_template_columns

 mis_template_row_mappings

 mis_data_snapshots

 mis_normalized_lines

 mis_ingestion_exceptions

 mis_drift_events

C. Schema Integrity Verification
Check actual DB metadata, not just ORM.

 column names match model definitions

 nullability matches intended design

 defaults exist where expected

 JSONB columns are typed correctly

 numeric precision/scale matches design

 FK references point to correct targets

 status/check constraints are present

 unique constraints are present

Special attention:

 version_token uniqueness

 snapshot_token uniqueness

 version_no uniqueness per template

 section_order uniqueness per template version

 ordinal_position uniqueness per template version

 line_no uniqueness per snapshot

D. Append-Only Verification
For append-only tables, attempt direct update and confirm rejection.

Tables to verify:

 mis_templates if treated append-only

 mis_template_versions

 mis_template_sections

 mis_template_columns

 mis_template_row_mappings

 mis_data_snapshots

 mis_normalized_lines

 mis_ingestion_exceptions

 mis_drift_events

Checks:

 update blocked

 delete blocked if platform doctrine requires it

 inserts still allowed

 append-only registry includes all intended tables

 no repository method bypasses append-only policy

If any table is intentionally allowed limited updates, document exact reason and exact allowed fields.

E. Supersession Trigger Verification
This is critical.

For mis_template_versions, verify all fail/allow paths in real DB.

Allowed:

 valid linear supersession chain

 valid candidate to active promotion path if supported by design

Rejected:

 self-supersession

 superseding across different templates

 cycle creation

 branching from same superseded parent

 multiple active versions for same template

 malformed supersedes reference

Need real DB assertions for error codes/messages where possible.

F. Snapshot Idempotency Verification
Use identical input twice.

Verify:

 same file hash

 same template version

 same reporting period

 same mapping state

 same validation rule set

 same resulting snapshot_token

Then verify behavior:

 second upload does not corrupt state

 duplicate normalized lines are not created incorrectly

 repository behavior is deterministic

 API behavior is deterministic

 repeated request returns stable outcome

Also test changed-input case:

 same template but changed file content produces different snapshot token when intended

G. RLS Verification
This is mandatory and must be real.

Test at least two tenants.

Verify:

 tenant A can read own MIS records

 tenant A cannot read tenant B records

 tenant A cannot insert rows scoped to tenant B

 tenant A cannot update tenant B rows

 tenant A cannot resolve drift/exception of tenant B

 FORCE RLS is active on all MIS tables

 service account behavior is understood and documented

 no accidental bypass through repository or policy layer

This should be tested through both:

direct DB session level

application/repository level

H. Control-Plane Enforcement Verification
For the API layer, verify all expected denials and allows.

Required checks:

 missing context token denied

 invalid context token denied

 module not enabled denied

 RBAC missing denied

 quota denied if applicable

 tenant routing failure denied

 correct permission allows request

 mis_manager module code is used consistently

Endpoints to verify:

 POST /mis/templates/detect

 POST /mis/templates/commit-version

 POST /mis/snapshots/upload

 POST /mis/snapshots/{id}/validate

 POST /mis/snapshots/{id}/finalize

 GET /mis/templates

 GET /mis/templates/{id}/versions

 GET /mis/snapshots/{id}

 GET /mis/snapshots/{id}/exceptions

 GET /mis/drift-events/{id}

 GET /mis/snapshots/{id}/normalized-lines

 GET /mis/snapshots/{id}/summary

I. Repository Verification
Inspect and test repository.py under real Postgres.

Checklist:

 every write path includes tenant scoping

 no hidden update paths exist

 version resolution is deterministic

 active template lookup is deterministic

 snapshot lookup is deterministic

 no “best effort” fallback that could cause silent misbehavior

 no broad unscoped query is used

 exceptions are appended, not overwritten

J. Deterministic Data Path Verification
Use a fixed fixture file and verify repeated execution.

 same detected header row

 same section detection

 same signature hashes

 same version token

 same snapshot token

 same normalized line count

 same normalized line ordering

 same exception set

 same drift decision outcome

If any output changes run-to-run, Phase 1F.1 is not closed.

K. Isolation Verification Against Accounting Engines
This is a must.

Verify:

 no inserts into revenue tables

 no inserts into lease tables

 no inserts into prepaid tables

 no inserts into fixed_assets tables

 no schedule regeneration is triggered

 no journal rows are created

 no FX rate service dependence exists in MIS flow

This can be tested by:

DB table row count diff before/after MIS operations

mock/assertion at service boundary

grep/audit of import paths and repository writes

5. Commit / Tag Gate Criteria
Hard gate — all must be true
 migration applies on fresh Postgres cleanly

 live DB integration tests pass

 RLS verified end-to-end

 append-only enforcement verified in DB

 supersession trigger rules verified in DB

 snapshot idempotency verified in DB

 control-plane API enforcement verified

 no accounting engine side effects detected

 no unresolved structural bug in repository/policy layer

 deterministic fixtures stable across repeated runs

Soft gate — should be true before freeze
 error messages are clear and stable

 design doc matches actual implementation

 invariant doc matches actual migration behavior

 test names and coverage are readable

 any intentionally allowed mutation path is explicitly documented

If any hard gate fails, do not tag.

deterministic run-to-run instability

Any one of these is enough to stop progression.

This is no longer infra.
This is a real migration bug in 0012.

Root problem
alembic.op.execute() is being called with the wrong signature.

Error:

TypeError: execute() takes 2 positional arguments but 3 were given

file: backend/migrations/versions/0012_phase1f1_mis_manager.py

line around: 730

That usually means the migration is doing something like:

op.execute(sql, params)
or

op.execute(statement, bindparams)

But Alembic op.execute() expects a single executable object or SQL string, not extra positional params.

inspect the exact op.execute(...) calls in migration 0012

STEP 1 — Inspect and Fix Migration 0012
Open:

backend/migrations/versions/0012_phase1f1_mis_manager.py
Find every op.execute(...) call, especially near line ~730.

Expected problem pattern
Alembic op.execute() does not accept extra positional parameters the way some SQLAlchemy execute flows do.

So if migration currently uses patterns like:

op.execute(sql, params)
op.execute(statement, bindparams)
replace them with one of the correct approaches:

Correct approach A — inline SQL string
If values are static and safe:

op.execute("SQL HERE")
Correct approach B — use sa.text(...) with bound params
If parameters are needed:

from sqlalchemy import text

conn = op.get_bind()
conn.execute(
    text(\"\"\"
    ...
    \"\"\"),
    {\"key\": value}
)
Correct approach C — separate execute calls
If multiple statements are being passed awkwardly, split into separate op.execute(...) or conn.execute(...) calls.

Fix requirement
inspect all op.execute(...) in 0012, not just the first failure

normalize all invalid uses

keep migration logic semantically identical

do not weaken behavior

After fixing, ensure the migration is clean, deterministic, and compatible with Alembic runtime.

Phase 1F.2 — Reconciliation Bridge

Good. We now move to Phase 1F.2 — Reconciliation Bridge.

This phase is where the platform becomes operationally useful for finance teams, not just computationally correct.

What 1F.2 is supposed to do
1F.2 should connect these worlds:

GL

Trial Balance

MIS snapshots from 1F.1

financial statement views / summary views

later, engine outputs where relevant

Its job is not to “fix accounting.”
Its job is to detect, explain, track, and resolve differences in a controlled, append-only, drillable way.

So the real purpose is:

turn mismatches into structured reconciliation cases with evidence, exception tracking, reviewer workflow, and deterministic closure history.

Core boundary rule
This is very important.

Reconciliation Bridge must not:
mutate accounting engine tables

rewrite MIS snapshots

alter TB/GL source imports

create journals automatically

silently net off differences

mark things reconciled by overwriting prior states

Reconciliation Bridge may:
compare datasets

create reconciliation sessions

create reconciliation lines

classify differences

attach evidence references

raise exceptions

record reviewer decisions as append-only events

expose drillable summaries and extracts

This must remain a control layer, not a mutation layer.

What 1F.2 should cover
A. GL ↔ Trial Balance reconciliation
Basic accounting completeness check.

Questions:

do summed GL balances equal TB balances?

by account?

by period?

by entity?

by currency?

B. MIS ↔ TB reconciliation
Management numbers vs accounting numbers.

Questions:

does MIS revenue tie to TB revenue?

do major expense buckets tie?

what is mapped vs unmapped?

where are presentation differences vs actual breaks?

C. MIS ↔ Financial statement / summary layer
This is for board pack confidence later.

Questions:

is MIS EBITDA aligned to normalized financial view?

are key balance positions aligned?

are variances explainable?

D. Service-company / finance-control checks
This is where you add practical controls:

payroll to employee cost tie

rent schedule to rent expense tie

subscription tracker to software expense tie

prepaid amortization to opex tie

FAR depreciation to depreciation expense tie

That becomes very powerful later.

Architecture principle
1F.2 must sit above:

ingestion

MIS normalization

accounting engines

And create a reconciliation evidence layer.

That means we need append-only objects like:

reconciliation session

reconciliation scope

reconciliation line

reconciliation exception

reconciliation resolution event

reconciliation evidence link

Proposed 1F.2 schema direction
1. reconciliation_sessions
Top-level run.

Fields should include:

id

tenant_id

organisation_id

reconciliation_type

period_start

period_end

source_a_type

source_b_type

source_a_ref

source_b_ref

session_token

status

created_at

created_by

Examples of reconciliation_type:

gl_vs_tb

mis_vs_tb

mis_vs_financials

schedule_vs_gl

payroll_vs_gl

2. reconciliation_scopes
Optional finer grouping inside a session.

Useful for:

entity

BU

account range

section

currency

location

Fields:

id

tenant_id

session_id

scope_code

scope_label

scope_json

created_at

created_by

3. reconciliation_lines
The core table.

Each line should represent one comparable item at a chosen grain.

Fields:

id

tenant_id

session_id

scope_id

line_key

comparison_dimension_json

source_a_value

source_b_value

variance_value

variance_abs

variance_pct

currency_code

reconciliation_status

difference_type

materiality_flag

explanation_hint

created_at

created_by

difference_type examples:

missing_in_a

missing_in_b

value_mismatch

mapping_gap

timing_difference

classification_difference

fx_difference

aggregation_difference

4. reconciliation_exceptions
Formal exception records for lines needing action.

Fields:

id

tenant_id

session_id

line_id

exception_code

severity

message

owner_role

resolution_status

created_at

created_by

5. reconciliation_resolution_events
Append-only workflow history.

Fields:

id

tenant_id

session_id

line_id

exception_id

event_type

event_payload_json

actor_user_id

created_at

Examples:

exception_opened

reviewer_assigned

explanation_added

evidence_linked

accepted_as_timing

accepted_as_mapping_gap

escalated

resolved

reopened

This is where your append-only governance remains intact.

6. reconciliation_evidence_links
Drill path to supporting objects.

Fields:

id

tenant_id

session_id

line_id

evidence_type

evidence_ref

evidence_label

created_at

created_by

Evidence refs may point to:

MIS snapshot line

TB import line

GL canonical entry

prepaid schedule row

FAR depreciation row

lease liability row

uploaded source artifact

This is how you preserve drillability.

Deterministic rules for 1F.2
These must be locked.

Rule 1 — Same inputs, same reconciliation session token
If:

same period

same source references

same scope rules

same matching logic version

Then output must be the same.

Rule 2 — No silent matching rule changes
Matching logic version must be explicit.

Add something like:

matching_rule_version

tolerance_rule_version

Rule 3 — Resolution is append-only
Never mutate old reconciliation conclusions.
Record new events.

Rule 4 — Evidence must be drillable
A resolved line without evidence trail is weak.
Push toward evidence-linked closure.

Rule 5 — Materiality should be explicit
Do not bury immaterial vs material logic.
Store threshold used.

Matching logic design
This is the heart of reconciliation.

You need deterministic matching stages.

Stage 1 — Exact key match
Examples:

account + entity + period

metric + dimension + period

Stage 2 — Mapped match
Examples:

MIS bucket mapped to multiple TB accounts

one MIS revenue bucket tied to 3 GL accounts

Stage 3 — Tolerance check
Examples:

rounding difference

timing lag within threshold

Stage 4 — Exception classification
If still unmatched, classify reason.

This logic must be versioned.

Materiality framework
Do not hardcode one number.

Store rules like:

absolute threshold

percentage threshold

account-specific threshold

section-specific threshold

Example:

revenue mismatch > 0.5% = material

minor rounding under 1 unit = immaterial

This makes the system controllable.

1F.2 initial reconciliation types to build first
Do not overbuild all at once.

Phase 1F.2.1
GL vs TB
This is the most foundational.

Phase 1F.2.2
MIS vs TB
This becomes immediately useful for CFO workflows.

Phase 1F.2.3
Schedule vs GL controls
Examples:

depreciation schedule vs depreciation GL

prepaid amortization vs related expense GL

lease schedule vs lease interest/liability GL

That connects 1F.2 back to engines without contaminating them.

API surface for 1F.2 first cut
Keep it simple and operational.

Session creation
POST /reconciliation/sessions

Run comparison
POST /reconciliation/sessions/{id}/run

View results
GET /reconciliation/sessions/{id}

GET /reconciliation/sessions/{id}/lines

GET /reconciliation/sessions/{id}/exceptions

Workflow actions
POST /reconciliation/lines/{id}/explain

POST /reconciliation/lines/{id}/attach-evidence

POST /reconciliation/lines/{id}/resolve

POST /reconciliation/lines/{id}/reopen

Summaries
GET /reconciliation/sessions/{id}/summary

Control-plane requirements
Same discipline as before.

Every endpoint must enforce:

valid context token

module enabled = reconciliation_bridge

RBAC permission

quota check

tenant routing

organisation scoping

Suggested permissions:

reconciliation_session_create

reconciliation_run

reconciliation_view

reconciliation_exception_resolve

reconciliation_evidence_attach

reconciliation_review

What success looks like
At the end of 1F.2, the platform should be able to say:

“These 14 lines match”

“These 3 are timing differences”

“These 2 are mapping gaps”

“This depreciation mismatch ties to FAR schedule row X”

“This MIS revenue mismatch comes from unmapped account bucket Y”

“This exception was reviewed, evidenced, and resolved by user Z on date T”

That is a real finance operations tool.

Recommended next deliverables
We should do this in order:

Deliverable 1
Phase 1F.2 audit-grade design doc

Deliverable 2
Expanded schema with constraints and append-only rules

Deliverable 3
Matching logic versioning model

Deliverable 4
Exception/resolution workflow design

Deliverable 5
Codex-ready implementation prompt

Do not jump to code immediately.

Lock the design first, exactly like we did for 1F.1.

Use this next instruction:

“Prepare the full Phase 1F.2 Reconciliation Bridge audit-grade design document with schema, invariants, matching logic, workflow events, API surface, and Codex-ready implementation plan.”

That is the correct next step.

Compare two financial data sources

Full audit-grade design for Phase 1F.3 — Payroll / GL Normalization Layer

Good.
Below is the full audit-grade design for Phase 1F.3 — Payroll / GL Normalization Layer.

This is designed to fit exactly into your already frozen architecture:

Phase 1D.x accounting engines frozen

Phase 1F.1 MIS Manager frozen

Phase 1F.2 Reconciliation Bridge frozen

So 1F.3 must strengthen upstream data quality without contaminating any of those layers.

Phase 1F.3 — Payroll / GL Normalization Layer
Audit-Grade Design
1. Purpose
Phase 1F.3 creates the platform’s canonical normalization layer for two critical operational sources:

Payroll data

General Ledger dumps / transaction extracts

Its purpose is to take messy source files or source API payloads and convert them into a stable, append-only, tenant-isolated, drillable canonical representation that downstream modules can trust.

This layer exists so later modules do not have to repeatedly decode raw payroll and GL structures.

2. Why this phase matters
Without normalization:

reconciliation becomes brittle

MIS mapping becomes inconsistent

payroll-to-employee-cost checks become unreliable

schedule-to-GL controls become hard to automate

finance analytics become client-format dependent

With normalization:

one canonical structure supports many downstream uses

line-level drillability is preserved

source lineage remains intact

mapping logic becomes reusable

reconciliation quality improves materially

So this phase is not a cosmetic ETL layer.
It is the financial data contract layer.

3. Architectural position
Phase 1F.3 sits between:

Inputs
payroll exports

GL dumps

ERP transaction extracts

manual upload files

future accounting APIs

Outputs
canonical payroll lines

canonical GL lines

normalized dimension mappings

source lineage references

Consumers
Reconciliation Bridge (1F.2)

MIS Manager enhancements

ratio / variance engine

board pack feeder

future close-control workflows

future CFO assistant layer

It must not directly mutate:

accounting engine tables

MIS frozen snapshots

reconciliation frozen outcomes

4. Core design principles
The design must obey the platform doctrine.

Mandatory principles
append-only

deterministic normalization

raw input preserved

no in-place overwrite of normalized history

tenant isolation

control-plane enforcement

replayable outputs

mapping-version aware

drillable to source row / source artifact

no journal creation

no accounting engine mutation

5. Boundary rules
Payroll / GL Normalization Layer must NOT:
post journals

alter source uploads

overwrite prior normalized runs

silently reclassify historical lines

mutate accounting engine schedules

mutate reconciliation decisions

directly “fix” source data

bypass MIS or reconciliation controls

Payroll / GL Normalization Layer may:
ingest source files / payloads

detect source structure

apply deterministic mapping rules

normalize source rows into canonical lines

raise exceptions

preserve unmapped items

version mapping logic

create normalized run snapshots

expose canonical extracts

6. Scope of 1F.3
This phase should cover two separate but related normalization families.

1F.3A — Payroll Normalization
Convert payroll exports into canonical payroll lines.

1F.3B — GL Normalization
Convert GL / journal dump extracts into canonical GL lines.

These should share architecture, but not be merged into one vague model.

PART A — PAYROLL NORMALIZATION
7. Payroll normalization objectives
The payroll side should normalize data such as:

employee ID

employee name

payroll period

gross pay

basic pay

allowances

bonuses

overtime

employer contributions

employee deductions

payroll taxes

benefits

net pay

department / cost center / BU / location

legal entity

currency

This is not just for HR reporting.
It is for finance control and reconciliation.

Examples of downstream use:

payroll expense to GL tie

employee cost to MIS tie

employer contribution accrual checks

provision / bonus checks

department-level employee cost analysis

8. Payroll normalization challenges to design for
Payroll files vary heavily by provider and client.

Typical problems:

different column names for same concept

combined earning buckets

split deduction columns

missing cost center

multiple sheets

month labels in different formats

gross/net logic inconsistency

employee IDs missing or duplicated

legal entity embedded in free text

row totals mixed with detail rows

So this layer needs structure detection + mapping + exception handling.

9. Payroll canonical model
The platform needs a canonical vocabulary for payroll.

Canonical payroll dimensions
employee_code

employee_name

payroll_period

legal_entity

department

cost_center

business_unit

location

grade

designation

currency_code

Canonical payroll metrics
basic_pay

hra

allowances

bonus

commission

overtime

employer_pf

employer_esi

gratuity_provision

leave_encashment

payroll_tax

employee_pf

employee_esi

loan_deduction

other_deductions

gross_pay

total_deductions

employer_total_cost

net_pay

This dictionary must be extendable but controlled.

PART B — GL NORMALIZATION
10. GL normalization objectives
The GL side should normalize raw transaction exports into canonical finance lines.

Key fields usually include:

journal ID

line number

posting date

document date

account code

account description

debit

credit

signed amount

currency

legal entity

cost center

department

project

customer

vendor

reference numbers

narration / memo

source module

source document ID

This becomes the canonical transaction base for reconciliation and analytics.

11. GL normalization challenges
GL dumps also vary heavily:

single amount vs debit/credit split

local currency vs transaction currency

period embedded in text

dimensions split across columns or concatenated

vendor/customer IDs inconsistently named

multiple header rows

subtotal rows

inconsistent account codes

missing signed amount logic

null dimensions

ERP-specific oddities

So this layer must normalize structure without losing raw lineage.

12. Canonical GL model
Canonical GL dimensions
legal_entity

posting_period

posting_date

document_date

account_code

account_name

cost_center

department

business_unit

project

product_line

customer

vendor

source_module

source_document_id

journal_id

journal_line_no

currency_code

Canonical GL metrics
debit_amount

credit_amount

signed_amount

local_amount

transaction_amount

This gives downstream modules one stable transaction contract.

COMMON NORMALIZATION ARCHITECTURE
13. Normalization lifecycle
Every normalization flow should follow this lifecycle:

Step 1 — Source intake
file or API payload received

source artifact recorded

source hash computed

tenant / org / user / source type captured

Step 2 — Structure detection
detect columns

detect sheet / block

detect header row

detect row grain

detect source type family

Step 3 — Mapping resolution
source fields mapped to canonical fields

mapping version selected

unmapped items flagged

Step 4 — Validation
required columns present

row-level numeric consistency

grain integrity

duplicate key checks

mandatory dimensions check

Step 5 — Normalization run freeze
create immutable normalization run

store canonical normalized lines

store exceptions

preserve source lineage

Step 6 — Downstream extract readiness
expose canonical lines to reconciliation / MIS / analytics

14. Required database schema
This is where the phase becomes real.

14.1 normalization_sources
Logical registration of a normalization source family.

Fields:

id

tenant_id

source_family

source_name

status

created_at

created_by

Examples of source_family:

payroll

gl

erp_gl_api

payroll_provider_export

Purpose:
logical parent for related source templates / mappings.

Versioned source structure definitions.

Fields:

supersedes_id

status

created_at

created_by

Rules:

append-only

one active version per source

no branching

no cycles

deterministic version token

This mirrors your MIS and engine discipline.

14.3 normalization_mappings

Fields:

This is the heart of the normalization layer.

deterministic run token

append-only

same inputs should produce same run token

run_type examples:

payroll_normalization

gl_normalization

better to normalize as line-level fact rows than wide frozen tables.

This lets the user drill from normalized line back to:

source row

raw payload block

import artifact

15. Append-only rules
Append-only must be enforced on:

normalization_source_versions

normalization_mappings

normalization_runs

payroll_normalized_lines

gl_normalized_lines

normalization_exceptions

normalization_evidence_links

If you later need review decisions, do that with new event tables, not row mutation.

16. Deterministic rules
These are mandatory.

Rule 1 — Same source + same mapping + same period = same run token
No randomness.

Rule 2 — Normalization output ordering must be stable
Ordering should use something like:

source row order

source column order

canonical field order

id as tie-breaker where needed

Rule 3 — Historical normalized output cannot be silently reinterpreted
If mapping changes, create a new version and a new run.

Rule 4 — Unmapped data must be explicit
Never silently drop source information.

Rule 5 — Signed amount logic must be deterministic
For GL especially:

if debit/credit provided, signed amount logic must be locked

no hidden sign inversion

17. Validation rules
You asked for full detail, so here are the practical validations.

Payroll validation rules
employee code or employee name anchor must exist

payroll period must be identifiable

amount fields must be numeric

gross/net relationships may be validated if enough fields exist

duplicate employee + period + metric combinations flagged

missing legal entity flagged where required

missing department / cost center flagged where configured mandatory

unmapped pay components flagged

summary rows must not be treated as employee detail rows

hidden sheets ignored unless explicitly configured

GL validation rules
account code or account name anchor must exist

posting date or posting period anchor must exist

signed amount must resolve deterministically

debit/credit inconsistency flagged

duplicate journal + line combinations flagged

missing legal entity flagged

null account code flagged where required

invalid numeric format flagged

subtotal rows excluded from transaction grain

currency inconsistency flagged if relevant

18. Mapping logic design
Mapping logic must be version-aware and deterministic.

Mapping layers
source structure mapping

canonical field mapping

transformation rules

default / fallback rules

mandatory field validation

Transform rule examples
trim text

uppercase account code

parse date format

split combined field

derive signed amount from debit/credit

map free-text pay component to canonical metric

map vendor dimension from alternate source column

Every transform rule must be:

explicit

testable

version-aware

No hidden heuristics in production path.

19. AI usage boundary
AI can help, but only as assistant.

AI may help with:
probable column identification

mapping suggestions

semantic similarity proposals

confidence scoring

AI must not:
auto-commit mapping changes

silently alter history

override hard validation rules

write final normalized rows without deterministic approval path

AI is not the authority.
Mapping version + deterministic rules are the authority.

20. Control-plane enforcement
Every endpoint and run must require:

valid context token

module enabled = payroll_gl_normalization

RBAC permission

quota availability

tenant routing

organisation scoping

Suggested permissions:

normalization_source_create

normalization_mapping_review

normalization_run_create

normalization_run_view

normalization_exception_resolve

normalization_extract_view

21. API surface
Keep phase 1F.3 operational and clean.

Source / template endpoints
POST /normalization/sources/detect

POST /normalization/sources/commit-version

GET /normalization/sources

GET /normalization/sources/{id}/versions

Run endpoints
POST /normalization/runs/upload

POST /normalization/runs/{id}/validate

POST /normalization/runs/{id}/finalize

GET /normalization/runs/{id}

GET /normalization/runs/{id}/exceptions

Extract endpoints
GET /normalization/runs/{id}/payroll-lines

GET /normalization/runs/{id}/gl-lines

GET /normalization/runs/{id}/summary

No mutation endpoints for normalized history.

22. Index strategy
Index only what you need for predictable performance.

Suggested indexes
source by tenant + code

source version by source_id + active status

run by tenant + source_id + reporting_period

run by run_token unique

payroll lines by run_id

payroll lines by employee_code + payroll_period

GL lines by run_id

GL lines by account_code + posting_period

exceptions by run_id + severity

evidence links by run_id + normalized_line_id

Avoid unbounded JSON scans where possible.

migration applies cleanly

Phase 1f3 Payroll Gl Normalization Master Prompt

🔐 PHASE 1F.3 — PAYROLL / GL NORMALIZATION LAYER
Full Audit-Grade Master Prompt (Complete 1–29 Components, No Omissions)
1. PURPOSE
Phase 1F.3 creates the platform’s canonical normalization layer for two critical operational source families:

Payroll data

General Ledger dumps / transaction extracts

Its purpose is to convert inconsistent source files and future source API payloads into a stable, append-only, tenant-isolated, deterministic, drillable canonical representation that downstream modules can trust.

This layer exists so later modules do not need to repeatedly decode raw payroll and GL source formats.

2. WHY THIS PHASE MATTERS
Without normalization:

reconciliation becomes brittle

MIS mapping becomes inconsistent

payroll-to-employee-cost checks become unreliable

schedule-to-GL controls become hard to automate

finance analytics become client-format dependent

With normalization:

one canonical structure supports many downstream uses

line-level drillability is preserved

source lineage remains intact

mapping logic becomes reusable

reconciliation quality improves materially

This is not a cosmetic ETL layer. It is the financial data contract layer for payroll and GL source families.

3. ARCHITECTURAL POSITION
Phase 1F.3 sits between:

Inputs
payroll exports

GL dumps

ERP transaction extracts

manual upload files

future accounting APIs

Outputs
canonical payroll lines

canonical GL lines

normalized dimension mappings

source lineage references

Consumers
Reconciliation Bridge (Phase 1F.2)

MIS Manager enhancements

Ratio & Variance Engine (future)

Board Pack feeder layer (future)

Close-control workflows (future)

CFO assistant layer (future)

This phase must not directly mutate:

accounting engine tables

MIS frozen snapshots

reconciliation frozen outcomes

4. CORE DESIGN PRINCIPLES
The design must obey the platform doctrine.

Mandatory principles
append-only

deterministic normalization

raw input preserved

no in-place overwrite of normalized history

tenant isolation

control-plane enforcement

replayable outputs

mapping-version aware

drillable to source row / source artifact

no journal creation

no accounting engine mutation

no reconciliation-state mutation

stable ordering of normalized outputs

explicit exception handling

explicit unmapped capture

5. BOUNDARY RULES
Payroll / GL Normalization Layer must NOT:
post journals

alter source uploads

overwrite prior normalized runs

silently reclassify historical lines

mutate accounting engine schedules or tables

mutate reconciliation decisions or frozen session outcomes

directly “fix” source data

bypass MIS or reconciliation controls

silently drop unmapped source information

introduce hidden transform rules

Payroll / GL Normalization Layer may:
ingest source files / payloads

detect source structure

apply deterministic mapping rules

normalize source rows into canonical lines

raise exceptions

preserve unmapped items explicitly

version mapping logic

create normalized run snapshots

expose canonical extracts

preserve evidence and raw lineage

6. SCOPE OF 1F.3
This phase covers two separate but related normalization families.

1F.3A — Payroll Normalization
Convert payroll exports into canonical payroll lines.

1F.3B — GL Normalization
Convert GL / journal dump extracts into canonical GL lines.

They should share architecture and governance, but they must not be collapsed into one vague structure that weakens auditability.

PART A — PAYROLL NORMALIZATION
7. PAYROLL NORMALIZATION OBJECTIVES
The payroll side should normalize data such as:

employee ID

overtime

employee deductions

benefits

net pay

department

This exists for finance control and reconciliation, not just HR reporting.

Downstream uses include:

payroll expense to GL tie

employee cost to MIS tie

employer contribution accrual checks

bonus/provision checks

department-level employee cost analysis

8. PAYROLL NORMALIZATION CHALLENGES TO DESIGN FOR
Payroll files vary heavily by provider and client.

Typical problems:

different column names for the same concept

combined earning buckets

split deduction columns

missing cost center

multiple sheets

month labels in different formats

gross/net logic inconsistency

employee IDs missing or duplicated

legal entity embedded in free text

row totals mixed with detail rows

multiple payroll cycles in one extract

YTD and monthly values mixed together

So this layer needs structure detection, mapping, validation, versioning, and exception handling.

COMMON NORMALIZATION ARCHITECTURE
13. NORMALIZATION LIFECYCLE
Every normalization flow must follow this lifecycle:

Step 1 — Source intake
file or API payload received

source artifact recorded

source hash computed

tenant / org / user / source type captured

Step 2 — Structure detection
detect columns

detect sheet / block

detect header row

detect row grain

detect source type family

Step 3 — Mapping resolution
source fields mapped to canonical fields

mapping version selected

unmapped items flagged

Step 4 — Validation
required columns present

row-level numeric consistency

grain integrity

duplicate key checks

mandatory dimensions check

Step 5 — Normalization run freeze
create immutable normalization run

store canonical normalized lines

store exceptions

preserve source lineage

Step 6 — Downstream extract readiness
expose canonical lines to reconciliation / MIS / analytics

No silent fallback logic is allowed.

15. APPEND-ONLY RULES

normalization_source_versions

gl_normalized_lines

normalization_exceptions

normalization_evidence_links

If review decisions are needed later, use new event tables rather than mutating rows.

16. DETERMINISTIC RULES
Rule 1 — Same source + same mapping + same period = same run token
No randomness.

Rule 2 — Normalization output ordering must be stable
Ordering should use:

source row order

source column order

canonical field order

id as tie-breaker only where needed

Rule 3 — Historical normalized output cannot be silently reinterpreted
If mapping changes, create a new version and a new run.

Rule 4 — Unmapped data must be explicit
Never silently drop source information.

Rule 5 — Signed amount logic must be deterministic
For GL especially:

if debit/credit provided, signed amount logic must be locked

no hidden sign inversion

17. VALIDATION RULES
Payroll validation rules
employee code or employee name anchor must exist

payroll period must be identifiable

amount fields must be numeric

gross/net relationships may be validated if enough fields exist

duplicate employee + period + metric combinations flagged

missing legal entity flagged where required

missing department / cost center flagged where configured mandatory

unmapped pay components flagged

summary rows must not be treated as employee detail rows

hidden sheets ignored unless explicitly configured

mixed monthly/YTD data must be flagged if ambiguous

GL validation rules
account code or account name anchor must exist

posting date or posting period anchor must exist

signed amount must resolve deterministically

debit/credit inconsistency flagged

duplicate journal + line combinations flagged

missing legal entity flagged

null account code flagged where required

invalid numeric format flagged

subtotal rows excluded from transaction grain

currency inconsistency flagged if relevant

reversal/batch total ambiguity flagged where detected

18. MAPPING LOGIC DESIGN
Mapping logic must be version-aware and deterministic.

Mapping layers
source structure mapping

canonical field mapping

transformation rules

default / fallback rules

mandatory field validation

Transform rule examples
trim text

uppercase account code

parse date format

split combined field

derive signed amount from debit/credit

map free-text pay component to canonical metric

map vendor dimension from alternate source column

Every transform rule must be:

explicit

testable

version-aware

deterministic

No hidden heuristics in the production path.

19. AI USAGE BOUNDARY
AI can assist, but only as assistant.

AI may help with:
probable column identification

mapping suggestions

semantic similarity proposals

confidence scoring

AI must not:
auto-commit mapping changes

silently alter history

override hard validation rules

write final normalized rows without deterministic approval path

AI is not the authority. Mapping version + deterministic rules are the authority.

payroll GL reconciliation is a seaparate module right? and all the next phases are separate modules right

Excellent question.
This is where architecture discipline matters.

Short answer:

Yes — payroll ↔ GL reconciliation should be a separate module.
And yes — all next phases must be separate modules.

But let me explain properly so we don’t blur boundaries.

1️⃣ Where Payroll GL Reconciliation Belongs
You now have:

1F.1 → MIS Manager

1F.2 → Reconciliation Bridge (generic engine)

1F.3 → Payroll / GL Normalization

Payroll ↔ GL reconciliation is NOT part of normalization.

It is also NOT part of the generic reconciliation engine core.

It is:

A reconciliation use-case built on top of the generic reconciliation bridge.

So structurally:

Normalization Layer (1F.3)
      ↓
Reconciliation Bridge Core (1F.2)
      ↓
Payroll-GL Reconciliation Module (use-case layer)
Meaning:

1F.2 provides the framework

Payroll-GL reconciliation is a configured specialization

So yes — it should be its own module.

2️⃣ Why Payroll GL Reconciliation Must Be Separate
Because payroll reconciliation involves domain-specific logic:

employer contributions tie logic

gross-to-net control logic

employer cost vs GL expense mapping

accrual checks

bonus provisioning checks

payroll tax controls

headcount cross-check

cost center tie-outs

month-on-month payroll delta checks

That is not generic reconciliation logic.

If you embed it into 1F.2, you contaminate the bridge.

The bridge should remain:

comparison engine

matching logic engine

variance engine

exception engine

Not domain-heavy payroll logic.

So:

Payroll GL Reconciliation = separate module that uses the bridge.

3️⃣ Clean Modular Map Going Forward
Here’s the correct structural layering.

Core Financial Engines (Frozen)
Revenue

Lease

Prepaid

Fixed Assets

Data Contract Layer
1F.1 MIS Manager

1F.3 Payroll / GL Normalization

Control Layer
1F.2 Reconciliation Bridge (generic framework)

Domain-Specific Reconciliation Modules
Separate modules:

Payroll ↔ GL Reconciliation

FAR ↔ GL Reconciliation

Lease ↔ GL Reconciliation

Prepaid ↔ GL Reconciliation

Revenue ↔ GL Reconciliation

MIS ↔ TB Reconciliation (already enabled via 1F.2)

Each of these must be modular.

Insight Layer (Future)
Ratio & Variance Engine

Close Control Engine

Risk Scoring Engine

CFO Assistant Layer

Each separate.

4️⃣ Why This Modular Discipline Matters
If you mix modules:

testing becomes messy

freeze points become unclear

regression surface grows

domain rules contaminate infrastructure

AI layers get messy context

governance weakens

If you separate modules:

freeze per module

commit per module

tag per module

regression isolation

audit clarity

monetization flexibility later

You can even productize modules separately.

5️⃣ So What Should Happen After 1F.3?
Correct structure:

Phase 1F.3 — Payroll / GL Normalization
(foundation layer)

Then:

Phase 1F.3.1 — Payroll ↔ GL Reconciliation Module
(domain module built on 1F.2 + 1F.3)

Then possibly:

Phase 1F.4 — Ratio & Variance Engine
(separate insight module)

6️⃣ Important Clarification
When you say:

“Are all next phases separate modules?”

The answer is:

Yes — unless they are infrastructure extensions.

Infrastructure examples (not separate business modules):

shared token builder

shared validation utilities

shared mapping registry

shared exception base classes

Everything domain-specific must be separate.

7️⃣ Architectural Rule Going Forward
You should now adopt this permanent rule:

No new business capability shall modify an existing frozen module unless it is a bug fix.

Every new capability:

separate module

separate migration

separate test suite

separate freeze tag

That keeps your platform enterprise-grade.

Phase 1F.3.1 — Payroll ↔ GL Reconciliation Module
Audit-grade design direction
1. What this module is
This module is a specialized finance-control module for reconciling:

normalized payroll outputs

normalized GL outputs

It should use:

1F.3 normalized payroll lines

1F.3 normalized GL lines

1F.2 reconciliation session / line / exception / evidence framework

So this module is not:

a new generic reconciliation engine

a new normalization module

a payroll processing engine

It is a domain-specific reconciliation layer.

2. Why it must be separate
Because payroll ↔ GL logic contains specialized business rules such as:

payroll expense tie-out

employer contribution tie-out

net pay clearing checks

payroll tax payable checks

bonus / variable pay accrual checks

headcount-linked cost anomalies

cost center mapping issues

timing differences between payroll run and GL posting

entity-wise payroll booking completeness

Those rules do not belong inside:

generic reconciliation core

generic normalization layer

So yes — this should be a separate module.

3. Architectural position
The correct stack is:

1F.3 Payroll / GL Normalization
        ↓
1F.2 Reconciliation Bridge Core
        ↓
1F.3.1 Payroll ↔ GL Reconciliation Module
This module should:

prepare payroll-specific comparison scopes

prepare payroll-specific matching logic

classify payroll-specific exceptions

use the Reconciliation Bridge tables/workflow

attach payroll/GL evidence links

4. What this module should do
At minimum, it should support:

A. Payroll total vs GL payroll expense
compare total normalized payroll cost

compare by period

compare by entity

compare by department / cost center where available

B. Earnings components vs GL booking buckets
Examples:

salary expense

bonus expense

overtime expense

employer PF/ESI

payroll tax

C. Net pay and payable control checks
payroll net pay vs payable / clearing account

unpaid payroll amount checks

liability balance mismatches

D. Employer contribution checks
employer PF / ESI / social contributions

payroll output vs GL accrual/expense/payable

E. Timing difference classification
payroll processed this month but booked next month

accrual reversed in next period

payment vs expense timing mismatch

F. Mapping gap detection
payroll component exists but no GL mapping

GL account exists but no payroll driver

cost center mismatch

5. Core design principles
This module must be:

append-only in its own decision/event layer

deterministic

evidence-linked

materiality-aware

drillable

tenant-isolated

control-plane enforced

separate from frozen 1F.2 core logic except allowed integration points

It must not:

post journals

modify normalized payroll lines

modify normalized GL lines

modify reconciliation core schema unless absolutely necessary and additive

alter payroll source data

alter GL source data

6. Suggested module boundary
Create as a separate module, for example:

backend/financeops/modules/payroll_gl_reconciliation/
  domain/
  application/
  infrastructure/
  api/
  policies/
  tests/
Do not bury payroll logic inside:

reconciliation_bridge

payroll_gl_normalization

Those remain foundational.

7. Recommended schema approach
Best approach:
Reuse 1F.2 reconciliation core tables for sessions, lines, exceptions, events, evidence.

Then add specialized configuration / mapping tables for payroll-GL domain logic.

Additive payroll-specific tables could include:
payroll_gl_reconciliation_mappings
Maps payroll canonical metrics to GL account groups.

Fields:

id

tenant_id

organisation_id

mapping_code

payroll_metric_code

gl_account_selector_json

cost_center_rule

entity_rule

effective_from

supersedes_id

status

created_at

created_by

payroll_gl_reconciliation_rules
Stores specific rule definitions.

Fields:

id

tenant_id

rule_code

rule_name

rule_type

tolerance_json

materiality_json

classification_behavior_json

effective_from

supersedes_id

status

created_at

created_by

payroll_gl_reconciliation_runs
Optional domain wrapper around generic reconciliation session if you want stronger payroll-specific tracking.

Fields:

id

tenant_id

organisation_id

reconciliation_session_id

payroll_run_id

gl_run_id

reporting_period

run_token

status

created_at

created_by

This depends on how strongly you want domain tracking.

My recommendation:
Use a lightweight domain wrapper table if you want future extensibility.

8. Payroll-specific matching logic
This is the heart of the module.

Matching should happen in stages.

Stage 1 — Direct aggregate tie
Match:

payroll metric total

mapped GL total

same entity

same period

Stage 2 — Cost center / department tie
Where available:

payroll department total

GL cost center/department total

Stage 3 — Component tie
Examples:

bonus → bonus expense GL

employer PF → statutory contribution GL

payroll tax → payroll tax payable / expense

Stage 4 — Timing-aware comparison
Use rules like:

same month exact

±N day grace window

accrual + reversal acceptance logic

Stage 5 — Classification
If mismatch remains, classify as:

timing_difference

mapping_gap

missing_gl_posting

missing_payroll_component

classification_difference

cost_center_mismatch

entity_mismatch

payable_mismatch

accrual_gap

This classification should be deterministic and versioned.

9. Materiality logic
Payroll mismatches can be noisy if you don’t materialize properly.

Use:

absolute threshold

percentage threshold

metric-specific threshold

entity-specific override

payroll-cycle-specific rule where needed

Examples:

total payroll mismatch > 0.25% = material

small rounding under 10 currency units = immaterial

employer contribution mismatch always flagged if statutory

10. Evidence model
Every payroll ↔ GL mismatch should be evidence-linked.

Evidence should point to:

normalized payroll lines

normalized GL lines

source payroll upload artifact

source GL upload artifact

reconciliation mapping rule used

rule version used

This is how you keep it drillable and auditable.

11. Exception workflow
Reuse the 1F.2 exception/event structure, but with payroll-specific event semantics.

Likely event types:

payroll_gl_exception_opened

mapping_gap_identified

timing_difference_accepted

evidence_attached

reviewer_confirmed

resolved_as_rounding

resolved_as_accrual_timing

escalated_to_finance

reopened

Append-only only.

No in-place overwrite of resolution history.

12. API surface
Keep this as a separate domain API.

Suggested endpoints:

Configuration
POST /payroll-gl-reconciliation/mappings

GET /payroll-gl-reconciliation/mappings

POST /payroll-gl-reconciliation/rules

GET /payroll-gl-reconciliation/rules

Run
POST /payroll-gl-reconciliation/runs

POST /payroll-gl-reconciliation/runs/{id}/execute

GET /payroll-gl-reconciliation/runs/{id}

GET /payroll-gl-reconciliation/runs/{id}/summary

Detail
GET /payroll-gl-reconciliation/runs/{id}/lines

GET /payroll-gl-reconciliation/runs/{id}/exceptions

POST /payroll-gl-reconciliation/lines/{id}/attach-evidence

POST /payroll-gl-reconciliation/lines/{id}/resolve

POST /payroll-gl-reconciliation/lines/{id}/reopen

This can internally create/use 1F.2 reconciliation sessions, but externally it should feel domain-specific.

13. Control-plane permissions
Add payroll-specific permissions such as:

payroll_gl_reconciliation_run

payroll_gl_reconciliation_view

payroll_gl_reconciliation_mapping_manage

payroll_gl_reconciliation_rule_manage

payroll_gl_reconciliation_exception_resolve

payroll_gl_reconciliation_evidence_attach

Do not overload generic permissions unless you intentionally want broader rights.

14. Deterministic rules
Lock these:

Same payroll run + same GL run + same rule version + same mapping version = same run token

Same inputs = same reconciliation output

Classification logic must be versioned

Evidence linkage must be append-only

Historical mismatches cannot be silently reclassified

15. Validation rules
This module should validate before running:

payroll normalization run exists and is finalized

GL normalization run exists and is finalized

both belong to same tenant

reporting periods are compatible

entity scope is compatible

mapping set exists

rule set exists

required payroll metrics are mapped

duplicate active mappings are blocked

duplicate active rules are blocked

16. Tests required
Unit tests
payroll metric to GL selector matching

timing window logic

materiality classification

deterministic run token generation

exception classification logic

Integration tests
migration applies cleanly

RLS isolation works

cross-tenant access denied

same inputs create same payroll-GL reconciliation output

evidence links resolve correctly

no mutation of normalized source lines

no mutation of reconciliation bridge core history outside allowed use

no journal side effect

no accounting engine side effect

Hard gate
Postgres-backed suite green

full pytest green

module isolated

freeze tag only after pass

17. Best implementation approach
Do not rewrite 1F.2.

Do not copy reconciliation logic blindly.

Build:

payroll-specific mapping layer

payroll-specific orchestration service

payroll-specific classification service

payroll-specific API

payroll-specific tests

And delegate generic compare/session/evidence workflow to 1F.2 where appropriate.

That is the cleanest design.

🔐 PHASE 1F.3.1 — PAYROLL ↔ GL RECONCILIATION MODULE
Full Audit-Grade Design + Codex Master Prompt
1. WHAT THIS MODULE IS
Phase 1F.3.1 is a specialized finance-control module for reconciling:

normalized payroll outputs

normalized GL outputs

It is a domain-specific reconciliation layer built on top of:

Phase 1F.3 Payroll / GL Normalization Layer

Phase 1F.2 Reconciliation Bridge

This module is not:

a new generic reconciliation framework

a payroll engine

a source normalization engine

a journal generation layer

It is a payroll-finance control module.

2. WHY THIS MUST BE A SEPARATE MODULE
Payroll ↔ GL reconciliation contains domain-specific logic that does not belong in generic reconciliation infrastructure.

Examples:

payroll expense tie-out

employer contribution tie-out

bonus accrual checks

payroll tax payable checks

net pay clearing checks

cost center mismatch checks

headcount-linked anomaly flags

payroll booking completeness by entity

timing difference handling between payroll run and GL posting

These rules are payroll-specific and should not contaminate:

reconciliation_bridge

payroll_gl_normalization

accounting engine modules

So this must be a separate domain module.

3. ARCHITECTURAL POSITION
The correct architecture is:

Phase 1F.3 Payroll / GL Normalization
                ↓
Phase 1F.2 Reconciliation Bridge Core
                ↓
Phase 1F.3.1 Payroll ↔ GL Reconciliation Module

use normalized payroll lines from 1F.3

use normalized GL lines from 1F.3

use reconciliation session/line/exception/evidence/event mechanisms from 1F.2

add payroll-specific mapping, rules, orchestration, and classification

It must not modify frozen prior-phase business logic except via additive integration points.

A. Payroll total vs GL payroll expense
Compare:

total normalized payroll cost

mapped GL payroll expense

by period

by entity

by legal entity

by department / cost center where available

B. Payroll component vs GL bucket reconciliation
Examples:

basic pay → salary expense GL

bonus → bonus expense GL

overtime → wage/overtime GL

employer PF / ESI → statutory contribution GL

payroll tax → payroll tax payable / expense GL

C. Net pay and payable control checks
Compare:

payroll net pay

payroll payable / salary clearing account

unpaid payroll amount controls

liability balance mismatches

D. Employer contribution checks
Compare:

employer PF / ESI / social contribution outputs

relevant GL accrual / expense / payable balances

E. Timing difference classification
Support logic like:

payroll processed this month but booked next month

accrual posted this month and reversed next month

payment posted in different period than expense

F. Mapping gap detection
Detect:

payroll metric exists but no GL mapping

GL payroll-related account exists but no payroll driver

missing cost center mapping

entity mismatch

component classification gap
