8. PAYROLL-SPECIFIC MATCHING LOGIC
Matching must be deterministic and staged.

Stage 1 — Direct aggregate tie
Compare:

payroll metric total

mapped GL total

same entity

same period

same currency context if relevant

Stage 2 — Cost center / department tie
Where mappings allow:

payroll department / cost center totals

GL department / cost center totals

Stage 3 — Component tie
Examples:

bonus → bonus expense GL

employer PF → statutory contribution expense/payable GL

payroll tax → payroll tax liability GL

deductions / clearing impacts where applicable

Stage 4 — Timing-aware comparison
Use timing rules like:

same month exact

allowable ±N-day posting lag

accrual + reversal accepted across adjacent periods

payroll run date vs posting date logic

Stage 5 — Final classification
If mismatch remains, classify deterministically.

Allowed categories:

timing_difference

mapping_gap

missing_gl_posting

missing_payroll_component

classification_difference

cost_center_mismatch

entity_mismatch

payable_mismatch

accrual_gap

rounding_difference

unsupported_source_gap

All matching logic must be versioned.

9. MATERIALITY LOGIC
Payroll mismatches can be noisy. Materiality must be explicit.

Support:

absolute threshold

percentage threshold

metric-specific threshold

entity-specific override

payroll-cycle-specific override

statutory-item always-flagged rule

Examples:

total payroll mismatch > 0.25% = material

rounding < 10 currency units = immaterial

employer contribution mismatch always flagged if statutory

net pay payable mismatch always flagged above threshold

Materiality rules must be stored in rule configuration and applied deterministically.

10. EVIDENCE MODEL
Every payroll ↔ GL mismatch must be evidence-linked.

Evidence should point to:

normalized payroll lines

normalized GL lines

payroll source artifact

GL source artifact

mapping rule used

reconciliation rule used

reconciliation session / line IDs

source reference metadata

Use 1F.2 evidence infrastructure where possible.

Every resolved mismatch should remain drillable.

No evidence means weak auditability.

11. EXCEPTION WORKFLOW
Reuse 1F.2 exception + resolution event structures, but with payroll-specific semantics.

Recommended payroll-GL event types:

payroll_gl_exception_opened

mapping_gap_identified

timing_difference_accepted

evidence_attached

reviewer_confirmed

resolved_as_rounding

resolved_as_accrual_timing

resolved_as_mapping_gap

escalated_to_finance

reopened

Rules:

append-only only

no overwrite of prior resolution state

all reviewer actions recorded as events

12. API SURFACE
This must be a separate domain API.

Configuration endpoints
POST /payroll-gl-reconciliation/mappings

GET /payroll-gl-reconciliation/mappings

GET /payroll-gl-reconciliation/mappings/{id}/versions

POST /payroll-gl-reconciliation/rules

GET /payroll-gl-reconciliation/rules

GET /payroll-gl-reconciliation/rules/{id}/versions

Run endpoints
POST /payroll-gl-reconciliation/runs

POST /payroll-gl-reconciliation/runs/{id}/execute

GET /payroll-gl-reconciliation/runs/{id}

GET /payroll-gl-reconciliation/runs/{id}/summary

Detail endpoints
GET /payroll-gl-reconciliation/runs/{id}/lines

GET /payroll-gl-reconciliation/runs/{id}/exceptions

POST /payroll-gl-reconciliation/lines/{id}/attach-evidence

POST /payroll-gl-reconciliation/lines/{id}/resolve

POST /payroll-gl-reconciliation/lines/{id}/reopen

Externally it should feel payroll-specific, even if internally it delegates to 1F.2 reconciliation structures.

13. CONTROL-PLANE PERMISSIONS
Add dedicated permissions such as:

payroll_gl_reconciliation_run

payroll_gl_reconciliation_view

payroll_gl_reconciliation_mapping_manage

payroll_gl_reconciliation_rule_manage

payroll_gl_reconciliation_exception_resolve

payroll_gl_reconciliation_evidence_attach

Do not rely only on generic reconciliation permissions unless intentionally designed that way.

Control-plane enforcement must require:

valid context token

module enabled = payroll_gl_reconciliation

RBAC permission

quota validation where applicable

tenant routing

organisation scoping

14. DETERMINISTIC RULES
Lock these as invariants.

Same payroll run + same GL run + same mapping version + same rule version = same run token

Same inputs = same reconciliation output

Classification logic must be versioned

Evidence linkage must be append-only

Historical mismatches cannot be silently reclassified

Materiality outcome must be reproducible

Ordering of lines and exceptions must be deterministic

No fallback logic may silently change reconciliation meaning

15. VALIDATION RULES
Before execution, validate:

payroll normalization run exists

payroll normalization run is finalized/usable

GL normalization run exists

GL normalization run is finalized/usable

both belong to same tenant

organisation scope is compatible

reporting period is compatible

mapping set exists

rule set exists

required payroll metrics are mapped

duplicate active mappings are blocked

duplicate active rules are blocked

unsupported source combinations are rejected explicitly

missing statutory mappings are flagged where required

no ambiguous active supersession state exists

No “best effort” execution should be allowed if required configuration is missing.

no FX side effect if not relevant

🔐 PHASE 1F.4 — RATIO & VARIANCE ENGINE
Full Audit-Grade Design + Codex Master Prompt
1. WHAT THIS MODULE IS
Phase 1F.4 is a deterministic finance intelligence module that derives:

financial metrics

ratios

growth measures

variance measures

trend outputs

materiality-aware movement flags

It is the first true insight layer above your existing control and data foundation.

This module is not:

a journal engine

a source normalization layer

a reconciliation engine

a forecasting engine

a dashboard-only layer

It is a versioned financial metric computation and comparison engine.

2. WHY THIS MODULE MATTERS
You already have:

deterministic accounting engines

MIS normalization

payroll / GL normalization

reconciliation bridge

payroll ↔ GL reconciliation

Those give you correctness and control.

What 1F.4 adds is:

financial meaning

executive relevance

period movement analysis

KPI standardization

board-pack readiness

AI CFO context foundation

Without 1F.4, the platform can say:

what was normalized

what reconciled

what mismatched

With 1F.4, the platform can say:

revenue grew 12.4%

EBITDA margin declined 210 bps

payroll-to-revenue ratio worsened materially

working capital expanded because AR days increased

gross margin compression is driven by COGS outpacing revenue

That is a major platform upgrade.

3. ARCHITECTURAL POSITION
The correct architecture is:

Accounting Engines (1D.x)
        ↓
Normalization Layers (1F.1, 1F.3)
        ↓
Reconciliation Layers (1F.2, 1F.3.1)
        ↓
Phase 1F.4 Ratio & Variance Engine
This module must read from prior layers and derive insights.

It must not mutate:

accounting engine outputs

normalization outputs

reconciliation states

source uploads

4. THIS MUST BE A SEPARATE MODULE
Implement as a separate module, for example:

backend/financeops/modules/ratio_variance_engine/
Do not inject metric logic into:

reconciliation_bridge

payroll_gl_normalization

payroll_gl_reconciliation

MIS manager

accounting engines

Allowed additive touches only
API router registration

append-only registry extension if needed

control-plane permission registration

DB model registration if architecture requires it

Everything domain-specific must live in the new module.

5. WHAT THIS MODULE SHOULD DO
At minimum, it should support:

A. Metric derivation
revenue

gross profit

EBITDA

EBIT

PAT / net income if supported

payroll cost

SG&A

working capital components

liquidity measures

leverage-supporting base metrics where data exists

B. Ratio derivation
gross margin %

EBITDA margin %

EBIT margin %

PAT margin %

payroll to revenue %

SG&A to revenue %

COGS to revenue %

AR days

AP days

inventory days

cash conversion cycle

current ratio

quick ratio

debt-to-equity where supported

interest coverage where supported

operating cash conversion style measures where supported

C. Variance computation
current vs prior period

current vs prior year same period

actual vs budget

actual vs forecast

actual vs normalized baseline

actual vs reconciled baseline where relevant

D. Trend computation
monthly trend

quarterly trend

rolling 3/6/12 period trend

ratio trend

movement direction

slope-like directional outputs if supported

E. Materiality propagation
identify whether change is material

propagate materiality through dependent metrics

distinguish cosmetic vs meaningful movements

F. Drillable lineage
Every metric and variance output must be drillable to:

underlying normalized lines

supporting reconciliation outputs

source periods

metric definition version used

variance rule version used

6. CORE DESIGN PRINCIPLES
This module must be:

deterministic

append-only in computed outputs/history

version-aware

materiality-aware

drillable

tenant-isolated

control-plane enforced

reproducible

modular

extensible

It must not:

post journals

mutate inputs

overwrite prior metric results

silently redefine metric formulas

silently reclassify historical variances

bypass reconciliation status if dependency rules require reconciled inputs

8. VARIANCE TYPES TO SUPPORT
Support explicit variance types as first-class definitions.

Period comparison types
current_vs_prior_period

current_vs_prior_year_same_period

current_vs_budget

current_vs_forecast

current_vs_baseline

rolling_avg_vs_current

trailing_12_vs_prior_trailing_12

Comparison outputs
absolute variance

percentage variance

basis points change

favorable / unfavorable / neutral classification

material / immaterial classification

9. MATERIALITY FRAMEWORK
Materiality must not be hardcoded into one number.

It should support:

absolute threshold

percentage threshold

basis points threshold

metric-specific override

entity-specific override

ratio-specific override

board-reporting threshold

statutory / covenant-critical always-flagged metrics

Examples:

EBITDA change > 5% = material

gross margin change > 100 bps = material

payroll-to-revenue shift > 50 bps = material

AR days movement > 5 days = material

debt covenant metric breach = always material

Materiality outcome must be deterministic and stored with the result.

10. TREND LOGIC
Trend outputs should be explicit and versioned.

Support:

sequential trend

rolling 3-period average

rolling 6-period average

rolling 12-period average

YoY trend

moving ratio trend

directional change

inflection detection placeholder if kept deterministic

Trend should not be a vague chart artifact.
It must be stored as structured computed outputs.

11. DRILLABLE LINEAGE MODEL
Every metric output must support drill-through.

A user should be able to move from:

metric result
→ metric component set
→ normalized / reconciled source references
→ raw lineage

Lineage should point to:

normalized payroll lines

normalized GL lines

MIS normalized lines

reconciliation sessions/lines

accounting engine outputs if used

metric definition version

variance rule version

trend rule version

This is mandatory for trust.

13. APPEND-ONLY RULES
Append-only must be enforced on:

metric_definitions

metric_definition_components

variance_definitions

trend_definitions

materiality_rules

metric_runs

metric_results

variance_results

trend_results

metric_evidence_links

If updates are ever needed, use supersession/versioning, not overwrite.

14. DETERMINISTIC RULES
Lock these as invariants.

Same input scope + same definition versions + same period = same run token

Same inputs = same metric results

Same inputs = same variance results

Same inputs = same trend results

Historical metrics cannot be silently recomputed under new definitions

Materiality classification must be deterministic

Favorable/unfavorable classification must be deterministic and metric-aware

Ordering of outputs must be deterministic

No hidden fallback definitions allowed

15. FAVORABLE / UNFAVORABLE CLASSIFICATION
This must be metric-aware.

Example:

revenue increase = favorable

payroll cost increase = unfavorable

gross margin increase = favorable

AR days increase = unfavorable

AP days increase may be favorable or neutral depending on policy

current ratio increase may be favorable up to a point

So each metric definition should support directionality_rule.

Possible values:

higher_is_better

lower_is_better

neutral

contextual

16. VALIDATION RULES
Before running, validate:

required normalized data sources exist

required reconciliation dependency exists if metric requires reconciled source

reporting period exists

metric definition set exists

variance definitions exist

trend definitions exist if requested

materiality rule exists

all referenced component metrics are resolvable

no duplicate active definitions for same code

no ambiguous supersession states

no unsupported unit mismatch

budget/forecast baseline exists when requested

No best-effort silent fallback.

valid context token

What People Usually Forget in Ratio Engines
There are 3 subtle areas that often get missed:

1️⃣ Metric Dependency Graph
Some metrics depend on other metrics.

Example:

EBITDA depends on revenue + COGS + SG&A

payroll_to_revenue depends on payroll_cost + revenue

net_debt_to_EBITDA depends on net_debt + EBITDA

You must ensure:

deterministic evaluation order

no circular dependency

version-aware dependency resolution

explicit dependency validation before execution

If your design supports formula_json and definition components properly, this is fine.

Just make sure Codex enforces no circular definitions.

2️⃣ Reconciliation Awareness (Optional but Powerful)
Some metrics should optionally depend on reconciled data.

Example:

EBITDA based only on reconciled GL lines

Payroll ratio only when payroll ↔ GL reconciliation run is closed

AR days only when AR reconciliation is closed

You don’t have to enforce this in 1F.4,
but design should allow a future flag like:

requires_reconciled_state: true
You can add this later if not in v1.

3️⃣ Period Alignment Rules
Variance logic must handle:

different fiscal calendars

4-4-5 structures

missing periods

stub periods

partial month data

You don’t need to overbuild this now.
But design the baseline selector to allow flexibility.

Can You Update Later?
Yes — if you follow these rules:

Metric definitions are versioned.

Variance definitions are versioned.

Trend definitions are versioned.

Materiality rules are versioned.

No historical overwrite.

Supersession only.

Old metric_runs remain intact.

Then 1F.4 becomes safely evolvable.

If you violate that discipline,
you destroy trust in the system.

What You Must Not Do Later
Never:

modify a metric definition in place

recompute historical runs silently

change materiality thresholds without versioning

alter directionality rules without versioning

collapse definition history

As long as you freeze versions properly,
you can extend forever.

Nothing structurally dangerous is missing.

The design is intentionally:

modular

extensible

That is exactly how a finance platform should evolve.

What We Should Pre-Validate While Codex Runs 1F.4
When Codex returns, don’t just look at:

tests passed

migration passed

For 1F.4, we need to examine deeper structural correctness.

Here’s what we’ll check.

1️⃣ Metric Dependency Graph Safety
We must verify:

Metric definitions form an acyclic graph.

No metric indirectly references itself.

Dependency resolution order is deterministic.

Formula resolution is stable across runs.

If this is wrong, your engine will silently become unstable later.

2️⃣ Deterministic Token Stability
Run token must be derived from:

reporting period

scope

metric definition version token

variance definition version token

trend definition version token

materiality rule version token

If any hidden runtime factor leaks in, determinism breaks.

We will re-run the same metric run twice and compare:

metric_results

variance_results

trend_results

ordering

3️⃣ Materiality Propagation Logic
We need to verify:

Parent metric materiality depends on base metric materiality when required.

Basis point logic is correct.

Favorable/unfavorable logic respects directionality.

No “always favorable” bug exists.

4️⃣ Period Alignment Handling
Even in v1, we need to ensure:

Missing prior period is rejected deterministically.

Budget baseline missing → explicit error.

YoY when prior-year period missing → explicit error.

No silent zero-fill.

Silence here = corruption later.

5️⃣ Append-Only Enforcement
Metric definitions must not allow in-place update.

Check:

UPDATE blocked.

Supersedes chain enforced.

No branching.

No cycles.

Metric history must be immutable.

6️⃣ Cross-Module Isolation
We must verify:

No mutation in normalization tables.

No mutation in reconciliation tables.

No journal insertion.

No accounting engine invocation.

No FX rate access.

No cross-module side effects.

1F.4 must be read-only against upstream layers.

7️⃣ Performance Envelope (Important)
Even if tests pass, we must inspect:

Metric runs are not doing N+1 queries.

Variance computation does not scan entire ledger each time.

Trend computation is window-based, not brute-force repeated scans.

This becomes critical at scale.

ratio & variance outputs

It should not compute raw accounting.
It should not replace reconciliation.
It should interpret financial impact using deterministic, versioned risk logic.

What 1F.5 should do
At minimum:

1. Materiality propagation
If a base metric changes materially, propagate impact to dependent metrics.

Examples:

payroll-to-revenue ratio worsens because payroll increased faster than revenue

EBITDA margin compression caused by SG&A and payroll movement

AR days increase drives working capital risk

debt / EBITDA deterioration triggers leverage risk

2. Risk scoring
Assign deterministic risk scores to:

metric movements

variance patterns

unresolved reconciliations

payroll-related pressure

liquidity pressure

leverage pressure

margin pressure

working capital pressure

3. Risk classification
Classify risks into buckets like:

liquidity risk

profitability risk

margin compression risk

payroll cost risk

working capital risk

leverage / covenant risk

reconciliation dependency risk

data quality / source confidence risk

timing difference risk

structural business risk

4. Severity layering
Support:

info

low

medium

high

critical

5. Dependency-aware interpretation
A metric shift alone is not enough.
The engine should interpret:

isolated movement

repeated movement

compounding movement

cross-metric correlated movement

6. Risk roll-forward
Carry forward unresolved material risks across periods in append-only form.

Why 1F.5 before anomaly engine
Because anomaly detection without risk weighting creates noise.

A change may be unusual but not important.
A different change may be small in % terms but critical because it affects:

EBITDA margin

debt covenant

payroll intensity

liquidity

So 1F.5 gives you the financial importance model.

Then 1F.6 anomaly detection becomes much smarter.

Correct architecture
The stack now becomes:

Accounting Engines
    ↓
Normalization Layers
    ↓
Reconciliation Layers
    ↓
Ratio & Variance Engine
    ↓
Financial Risk & Materiality Propagation Engine (1F.5)
Later:

1F.5 Risk Engine
    ↓
1F.6 Anomaly & Pattern Engine
    ↓
1F.7 Board Pack & Narrative Engine
    ↓
AI CFO Layer
Key design rule
This must be a separate module.

For example:

backend/financeops/modules/financial_risk_engine/
Do not inject risk logic into:

ratio_variance_engine

payroll_gl_reconciliation

reconciliation_bridge

normalization modules

accounting engines

Only additive integration is allowed.

What I recommend for 1F.5 design choice
Between the three options I gave earlier, the strongest route is:

B) Deterministic + configurable risk weights per metric
Why:

stronger than pure fixed rules

still auditable

still deterministic

tenant/org configurable

future-ready for ML later without breaking governance

So 1F.5 should be:

deterministic

rule-based

weight-configurable

versioned

append-only

That is the sweet spot.

What we should design next
For 1F.5 we should lock:

risk definition registry

risk propagation rules

risk dependency graph

severity and score model

confidence model

unresolved-risk roll-forward model

evidence and lineage model

API surface

control-plane permissions

DB closure gates

commit/tag rules

🔐 PHASE 1F.5 — FINANCIAL RISK & MATERIALITY PROPAGATION ENGINE
Full Audit-Grade Design + Codex Master Prompt
1. WHAT THIS MODULE IS
Phase 1F.5 is a deterministic financial risk interpretation layer built above:

normalized data layers

reconciliation layers

ratio & variance outputs

Its purpose is to convert:

metric movements

ratio shifts

variance results

unresolved reconciliation states

source confidence conditions

into:

structured financial risks

propagated materiality impacts

severity classifications

dependency-aware risk chains

unresolved risk carry-forwards

This module is not:

a journal engine

a new reconciliation engine

a source normalization engine

a forecasting engine

a probabilistic black-box model

It is a versioned, deterministic, audit-grade risk engine.

2. WHY THIS MODULE MATTERS
You already have:

deterministic accounting engines

deterministic normalization

deterministic reconciliation

payroll ↔ GL reconciliation

deterministic ratio & variance engine

Those tell you:

what happened

by how much

whether it reconciled

whether a metric moved materially

What 1F.5 adds is:

why that movement matters financially

how risk propagates to dependent metrics

whether the issue is isolated or systemic

whether the issue is temporary, structural, or unresolved

what deserves CFO / board attention

which risks remain open across periods

Without 1F.5, the platform remains measurement-heavy.

With 1F.5, it becomes an actual financial risk intelligence platform.

3. ARCHITECTURAL POSITION
The correct architecture is:

Accounting Engines (1D.x)
        ↓
Normalization Layers (1F.1, 1F.3)
        ↓
Reconciliation Layers (1F.2, 1F.3.1)
        ↓
Ratio & Variance Engine (1F.4)
        ↓
Phase 1F.5 Financial Risk & Materiality Propagation Engine
Later:

Phase 1F.5 Risk Engine
        ↓
Phase 1F.6 Anomaly & Pattern Detection
        ↓
Phase 1F.7 Board Pack & Narrative Layer
        ↓
AI CFO Layer
This module must read prior outputs and derive risk interpretation.

It must not mutate:

accounting engine tables

normalized source outputs

reconciliation history

ratio/variance outputs

source uploads

4. THIS MUST BE A SEPARATE MODULE
Implement as a separate module, for example:

backend/financeops/modules/financial_risk_engine/
Do not inject risk logic into:

ratio_variance_engine

payroll_gl_reconciliation

reconciliation_bridge

payroll_gl_normalization

mis_manager

accounting engine modules

Allowed additive touches only
API router registration

append-only registry extension if required

control-plane permission registration

DB model registration if architecture requires it

Everything risk-domain-specific must live in the new module.

5. WHAT THIS MODULE SHOULD DO
At minimum it must support:

A. Risk creation from metric and variance outputs
Examples:

EBITDA margin compression risk

payroll intensity risk

working capital deterioration risk

liquidity pressure risk

leverage / covenant risk

gross margin compression risk

revenue slowdown risk

cost escalation risk

B. Materiality propagation
If a base metric movement is material, propagate impact to dependent risk nodes.

Examples:

payroll_to_revenue worsens materially

this contributes to EBITDA_margin pressure

which then contributes to operating performance risk

which may then elevate board-level concern if thresholds are crossed

C. Reconciliation-aware risk uplift
If source data is unresolved or reconciliation is open, risk confidence and/or severity can be affected deterministically.

Examples:

payroll mismatch unresolved → payroll expense confidence risk

AR metric based on unresolved inputs → working capital confidence risk

critical KPI derived from unreconciled source → elevated control risk flag

D. Severity classification
Support:

info

low

medium

high

critical

E. Configurable risk weighting
Weights should be configurable by:

metric

ratio

risk type

entity

tenant

rule version

But still deterministic.

F. Dependency-aware interpretation
The engine should recognize:

local risk

parent risk

propagated risk

correlated risk

unresolved inherited risk

G. Unresolved risk roll-forward
If risk remains unresolved in a prior period and persists into the next, it should carry forward append-only as a tracked risk lineage.

H. Drillable evidence and lineage
Every risk output should be drillable to:

metric result

variance result

reconciliation exception / session if relevant

normalized source lines if relevant

risk definition version

propagation rule version

weight configuration version

6. CORE DESIGN PRINCIPLES
This module must be:

deterministic

append-only

version-aware

dependency-aware

materiality-aware

tenant-isolated

control-plane enforced

evidence-linked

drillable

replay-safe

configurable but governed

It must not:

post journals

mutate upstream layers

silently redefine risk logic in place

silently re-score historical risks under new rules

use opaque probabilistic scoring in core execution path

perform hidden cross-module changes

7. RISK DOMAINS TO SUPPORT
At minimum, support these top-level risk domains.

7.1 Profitability risk
Examples:

EBITDA_margin compression

gross_margin compression

PAT deterioration

EBIT decline

contribution pressure

7.2 Cost structure risk
Examples:

payroll_to_revenue pressure

SG&A inflation

rent burden increase

software expense burden increase

employer contribution pressure

7.3 Liquidity risk
Examples:

current_ratio deterioration

quick_ratio deterioration

cash pressure

working capital tightening

7.4 Working capital risk
Examples:

AR days expansion

AP days compression

inventory days increase

CCC worsening

7.5 Leverage / coverage risk
Examples:

debt_to_equity deterioration

net_debt_to_EBITDA deterioration

interest coverage pressure

7.6 Payroll-specific financial risk
Examples:

payroll growth outpacing revenue growth

employer contribution mismatch

payroll concentration risk

bonus surge risk

cost-per-employee abnormality precursor

unresolved payroll reconciliation dependency risk

7.7 Reconciliation dependency risk
Examples:

KPI based on unresolved reconciliations

critical metric confidence impaired by open recon breaks

7.8 Data confidence / source trust risk
Examples:

metric computed from incomplete normalized runs

unsupported period baseline

missing mapped components

repeated source anomalies

8. RISK TYPES TO SUPPORT
Risk types should be explicitly modeled.

Examples:

metric_movement_risk

variance_risk

ratio_pressure_risk

propagation_risk

confidence_risk

reconciliation_dependency_risk

structural_risk

timing_risk

concentration_risk

trend_risk

threshold_breach_risk

covenant_risk

9. CONFIGURABLE RISK WEIGHT MODEL
Use deterministic configurable weights.

Support weights by:

risk definition

metric code

ratio code

variance code

entity

risk domain

period type

source confidence condition

board-critical flag

Example approach:

EBITDA_margin compression weight = 0.90

payroll_to_revenue deterioration weight = 0.75

unresolved payroll reconciliation dependency uplift = +0.20

covenant-risk metrics always weighted high

Weights must be:

versioned

explainable

deterministic

append-only when changed

10. MATERIALITY PROPAGATION MODEL
Materiality must flow through dependencies in controlled fashion.

Examples:

payroll_cost materially up

payroll_to_revenue materially worse

EBITDA materially down

profitability_risk severity elevated

Another example:

AR_days materially worse

working capital risk elevated

liquidity risk receives propagated uplift if cash is already weak

This should be rule-based, not vague.

Support:

parent-child dependency graph

propagation factor

attenuation or amplification factor

cap rules

severity escalation rules

confidence degradation if dependencies unresolved

11. DEPENDENCY-AWARE INTERPRETATION
Risk is not just isolated scoring.

The engine must be able to interpret:

a metric’s direct risk

inherited risk from dependencies

propagated materiality

repeated unresolved risk over periods

risk correlation across domains

Examples:

payroll_to_revenue worsening + EBITDA margin worsening = compounding cost-structure risk

AR_days worsening + current_ratio worsening = liquidity stress linkage

net_debt_to_EBITDA worsening + interest_coverage weakening = leverage pressure escalation

This should remain deterministic and definition-driven.

12. UNRESOLVED RISK ROLL-FORWARD
This is a major requirement.

If a risk remains unresolved:

it should persist to future periods

retain origin lineage

retain prior severity history

allow new events to escalate, reaffirm, or resolve it

This should be append-only, not overwritten.

Examples:

unresolved payroll mapping gap risk rolls forward for 3 periods

unresolved gross margin compression risk persists but worsens

unresolved liquidity warning becomes critical after repeated periods

13. DRILLABLE LINEAGE MODEL
Every risk output must support drill-through.

A user should be able to move from:

risk result
→ risk contributing signals
→ metric results
→ variance results
→ reconciliation outputs
→ normalized source lines
→ original source lineage

Lineage should include:

risk definition version used

propagation rule version used

weight configuration version used

source metric result IDs

source variance result IDs

source reconciliation refs where applicable

This is mandatory for trust and auditability.

15. APPEND-ONLY RULES
Append-only must be enforced on:

risk_definitions

risk_definition_dependencies

risk_weight_configurations

risk_materiality_rules

risk_runs

risk_results

risk_contributing_signals

risk_rollforward_events

risk_evidence_links

No in-place overwrite of historical risk meaning.

Use supersession/versioning only.

16. DETERMINISTIC RULES
Lock these as invariants.

Same inputs + same version tokens = same run token

Same inputs = same risk results

Same inputs = same severity outcomes

Same inputs = same confidence outcomes

Same inputs = same propagation outcomes

Historical risks cannot be silently rescored under new rules

Roll-forward must preserve lineage and history

Ordering of risk results must be deterministic

No hidden fallback rules are allowed

17. SCORE / SEVERITY MODEL
Keep scoring deterministic.

One recommended approach:

raw risk score from weighted contributing signals

severity bucket mapping from score thresholds

confidence score derived from source quality / reconciliation state / coverage

board_attention_flag from severity + domain + board relevance

Examples:

0.00–0.19 → info

0.20–0.39 → low

0.40–0.59 → medium

0.60–0.79 → high

0.80–1.00 → critical

This is just one model; Codex may implement a threshold-driven deterministic scheme using config tables.

18. CONFIDENCE MODEL
Risk output should include confidence, not just severity.

Confidence may be reduced if:

upstream reconciliation unresolved

source coverage incomplete

metric dependency missing

baseline unavailable

unsupported source selector used

Confidence classification can be:

high

medium

low

Or numeric, if deterministic and rule-backed.

19. BOARD ATTENTION MODEL
Some risks should escalate for executive attention.

Board/CFO attention should depend on:

severity

domain

persistence across periods

dependency on strategic metrics

covenant relevance

liquidity relevance

unresolved duration

This should be deterministic and configuration-backed.

20. VALIDATION RULES
Before execution, validate:

required metric runs exist

required variance runs exist

required trend runs exist if referenced

required reconciliation dependencies exist if configured

risk definitions exist

propagation dependencies are acyclic

weight configuration exists

materiality rule exists

no duplicate active definitions for same risk_code

no ambiguous supersession state

no unsupported dependency references

no circular dependency graph

no invalid propagation factor ranges

No best-effort silent fallback.

21. CONTROL-PLANE ENFORCEMENT
Every endpoint and run must require:

valid context token

module enabled = financial_risk_engine

RBAC permission

quota validation where applicable

tenant routing

organisation scoping

Suggested permissions:

Are version tokens locked into risk_runs?

If the answer to those is yes (and based on your tests, it appears so), then 1F.5 is architecturally sound.

🧱 What You Have Built So Far

Layer 1 — Transaction correctness

Layer 4 — Financial measurement
Layer 5 — Financial risk interpretation

That is a real architecture progression.

Very few platforms reach this structure.

🔐 PHASE 1F.6 — ANOMALY & PATTERN DETECTION ENGINE
Full Audit-Grade Design + Codex Master Prompt
1️⃣ WHAT THIS MODULE IS
Phase 1F.6 is a deterministic anomaly and pattern interpretation engine built above:

normalized finance data

reconciliation outputs

ratio & variance outputs

financial risk outputs

Its purpose is to identify:

unusual metric behavior

persistent deterioration

repeated risk signatures

correlated abnormal movements

structural breaks

trend discontinuities

control fatigue patterns

emerging business stress patterns

This module is not:

a stochastic ML anomaly engine

a black-box AI system

a source normalization layer

a reconciliation layer

a forecasting engine

a journaling module

It is a versioned, deterministic, audit-grade anomaly detection layer.

2️⃣ WHY THIS MODULE MATTERS
You already have:

correct accounting logic

normalized source data

reconciliation infrastructure

payroll ↔ GL controls

ratio & variance intelligence

financial risk propagation

Those layers tell you:

what changed

by how much

whether it is material

whether it creates risk

What 1F.6 adds is:

whether the change is abnormal

whether the movement is persistent

whether multiple signals are converging into a pattern

whether this is a one-period event vs structural shift

whether the issue is isolated vs correlated

whether the same anomaly signature is repeating over time

Without 1F.6, the platform is financially intelligent.
With 1F.6, the platform becomes pattern intelligent.

3️⃣ ARCHITECTURAL POSITION
The correct architecture is:

Accounting Engines (1D.x)
        ↓
Normalization Layers (1F.1, 1F.3)
        ↓
Reconciliation Layers (1F.2, 1F.3.1)
        ↓
Ratio & Variance Engine (1F.4)
        ↓
Financial Risk Engine (1F.5)
        ↓
Phase 1F.6 Anomaly & Pattern Detection Engine
Later:

Phase 1F.6 Anomaly & Pattern Detection
        ↓
Phase 1F.7 Board Pack & Narrative Layer
        ↓
AI CFO Layer
This module must read from prior layers only.
It must not mutate upstream state.

4️⃣ THIS MUST BE A SEPARATE MODULE
Implement as a separate module, for example:

backend/financeops/modules/anomaly_pattern_engine/
Do not inject anomaly logic into:

financial_risk_engine

ratio_variance_engine

payroll_gl_reconciliation

reconciliation_bridge

payroll_gl_normalization

mis_manager

accounting engine modules

Allowed additive touches only
API router registration

append-only registry extension if required

control-plane permission registration

DB model registration if architecture requires it

All anomaly-domain logic must remain isolated.

5️⃣ WHAT THIS MODULE SHOULD DO
At minimum it must support:

A. Point anomalies
Detect unusually high or low movement in a metric, ratio, or risk signal for a given period.

Examples:

payroll cost spike

sudden gross margin drop

AR days jump

EBITDA margin collapse

bonus expense surge

B. Persistent anomalies
Detect anomalies that continue across multiple periods.

Examples:

three-period payroll intensity deterioration

recurring working capital stress

margin compression repeating for 4 periods

C. Structural break detection
Detect when a trend meaningfully changes regime.

Examples:

revenue growth trend breaks from positive to negative

payroll trend jumps to a new cost base

liquidity weakens beyond historical threshold regime

D. Correlated anomalies
Detect when multiple metrics move abnormally together.

Examples:

payroll_to_revenue worsens + EBITDA margin worsens

AR days increases + current ratio declines

debt_to_EBITDA worsens + interest coverage weakens

E. Pattern signatures
Detect known deterministic patterns such as:

cost escalation pattern

liquidity squeeze pattern

margin compression pattern

payroll burden pattern

reconciliation fatigue pattern

statutory contribution inconsistency pattern

control breakdown precursor pattern

F. Roll-forward anomaly persistence
Track unresolved or repeating anomalies across periods.

G. Drillable evidence
Every anomaly must be explainable via underlying metric, variance, trend, and risk outputs.

6️⃣ CORE DESIGN PRINCIPLES
This module must be:

deterministic

append-only

version-aware

drillable

tenant-isolated

control-plane enforced

evidence-linked

trend-aware

risk-aware

pattern-aware

replay-safe

It must not:

post journals

alter upstream outputs

silently redefine anomaly logic

silently reclassify historical anomalies

use hidden heuristics in production path

perform black-box scoring

7️⃣ ANOMALY DOMAINS TO SUPPORT
At minimum support anomalies in these domains:

7.1 Profitability anomalies
EBITDA anomaly

margin compression anomaly

gross profit anomaly

PAT deterioration anomaly

7.2 Cost anomalies
payroll spike anomaly

SG&A spike anomaly

employer contribution anomaly

rent / software / marketing burden anomaly

7.3 Liquidity anomalies
current ratio anomaly

quick ratio anomaly

cash squeeze anomaly

7.4 Working capital anomalies
AR days anomaly

AP days anomaly

inventory anomaly

CCC anomaly

7.5 Leverage anomalies
debt-to-equity anomaly

net debt / EBITDA anomaly

interest coverage deterioration anomaly

7.6 Payroll-specific anomalies
payroll growth > revenue growth anomaly

payroll cost per employee anomaly

bonus concentration anomaly

payroll burden persistence anomaly

mapping-gap persistence anomaly

7.7 Reconciliation dependency anomalies
unresolved reconciliations repeatedly affecting key metrics

repeated dependency confidence degradation

7.8 Pattern deterioration anomalies
repeated medium risks compounding into a structural anomaly

repeated unresolved materiality event chain

8️⃣ ANOMALY TYPES TO SUPPORT
Model anomaly types explicitly.

Examples:

spike_anomaly

drop_anomaly

deviation_anomaly

persistence_anomaly

regime_shift_anomaly

correlation_anomaly

repeated_unresolved_anomaly

threshold_breach_anomaly

confidence_degradation_anomaly

pattern_signature_anomaly

control_fatigue_anomaly

created_by

no in-place overwrite

1️⃣8️⃣ MATERIALITY-AWARE ANOMALY INTERPRETATION

board-critical domain

4️⃣ ENHANCED STATISTICAL BASELINE LAYER (DETERMINISTIC)
Add deterministic statistical logic:

4.1 Rolling baseline support

rolling_mean

rolling_std

rolling_median (optional)

rolling_pct_change

Window sizes configurable via rule:

3

6

12

24 periods

4.2 Z-score anomaly logic
Compute deterministic z-score:

z = (current_value - rolling_mean) / rolling_std
Thresholds configurable:

|z| > 1.5 → moderate anomaly

|z| > 2.0 → high anomaly

|z| > 3.0 → extreme anomaly

Must be:

deterministic

based only on historical stored metric results

no randomness

no external ML model

4.3 Regime shift detection
Detect structural break if:

mean of last N periods deviates from prior N baseline by threshold %

sign of growth trend reverses

variance regime increases beyond baseline threshold

seasonal_period = 12

no freeform LLM dependency in core execution path

Template types:

executive_summary_template

metric_commentary_template

variance_commentary_template

risk_commentary_template

anomaly_commentary_template

board_attention_template

period_close_summary_template

Fields:

template_code

template_name

template_type

template_body_json or template_text

placeholder_schema_json

supersedes_id

status

effective_from

No in-place edits.

5️⃣ Versioned Inclusion Rules
Create table: board_pack_inclusion_rules

Purpose:

decide what gets included in a pack

threshold-driven deterministic inclusion

Examples:

include only material variances

include only high and critical risks

include only sustained anomalies

include top 5 issues by severity

include payroll section only if payroll materiality/risk triggered

Fields:

rule_code

rule_name

rule_type

inclusion_logic_json

supersedes_id

status

effective_from

6️⃣ Deterministic Run Token
Create table: board_pack_runs

Run token must hash:

reporting_period

organisation_id

board_pack_definition_version_token

section_definition_version_token

narrative_template_version_token

inclusion_rule_version_token

source_metric_run_ids

source_risk_run_ids

source_anomaly_run_ids

Same inputs → same run_token.

7️⃣ Deterministic Execution Order
Board-pack generation must be deterministic.

Execution order must be stable across:

section selection

summary ranking

narrative block assembly

evidence linking

issue ordering

No unordered DB scan dependence.

8️⃣ Section Assembly Engine
Create deterministic section assembly logic.

Each section should be assembled from:

metric results

variance results

risk results

anomaly results

reconciliation dependency status where relevant

Examples:

financial_performance section built from revenue, EBITDA, margin, payroll ratio

liquidity section built from current ratio, quick ratio, cash, CCC

risk section built from high/critical risk results

anomaly section built from recurring/sustained anomalies

9️⃣ Narrative Generation Engine
Narrative must be deterministic and template-backed.

No freeform generative text in core execution.

Use:

versioned templates

placeholder binding

rule-driven sentence assembly

deterministic grammar blocks

optional later AI assist outside core frozen path

Narrative examples:

“Revenue increased 8.2% MoM, while EBITDA margin declined 120 bps, primarily driven by payroll cost growth outpacing revenue.”

“Liquidity risk remains elevated due to sustained AR days expansion and a continued decline in current ratio.”

“Payroll intensity risk persisted for the third consecutive period and is now classified as high severity.”

🔟 Executive Summary Logic
Create deterministic executive summary generation.

Executive summary should:

prioritize most material performance movements

surface highest-severity risks

surface sustained anomalies

note unresolved roll-forward issues

produce concise CFO/board summary block

This should not be arbitrary.
Ordering and inclusion must be rule-based.

1️⃣1️⃣ Risk-Aware Summary Logic
Board-pack narrative must be risk-aware.

Examples:

if profitability risk high, explain key drivers

if liquidity risk high, elevate liquidity section priority

if payroll risk high, include payroll commentary

if reconciliation dependency risk high, mention confidence caveat

This must be deterministic and traceable.

1️⃣2️⃣ Anomaly-Aware Summary Logic
Anomaly summaries must:

include recurring anomalies

highlight sustained anomalies

flag correlated anomalies

suppress immaterial one-off noise when rule-configured

Examples:

recurring payroll burden anomaly

sustained liquidity stress pattern

repeated unresolved reconciliation anomaly

1️⃣3️⃣ Board Attention Flag Model
Board-attention items should be separately identified.

Create explicit logic that flags:

critical risks

board-critical anomalies

covenant-related deterioration

sustained multi-period deterioration

repeated unresolved issues

This should produce a dedicated section or subsection:

board_attention_items

1️⃣4️⃣ Multi-Period Persistence Logic
The board pack must be able to surface:

repeated issues over periods

unresolved risks carried forward

persistent anomalies

improving vs worsening issues

This requires reading roll-forward chains from 1F.5 and 1F.6.

1️⃣5️⃣ Drillable Evidence Ledger

risk result

anomaly result

reconciliation result if referenced

normalized source refs where relevant

narrative template version

board pack definition version

No opaque summary.

1️⃣9️⃣ No Upstream Mutation Guarantee

prompt seems to be missing items of 29 or it is briefly covered, do we need to improve prompt

Yes — it should be improved.

The current Phase 2.1 prompt is directionally correct, but for a non-functional refactor phase the risk is different from feature phases. Here, the real danger is not “missing a table,” it is silent drift.

So for 2.1, the prompt must be even stricter than the earlier feature prompts in five areas that are currently too compressed:

What is still too weak in the current prompt
1. Exact no-drift proof standard
It says “no-drift,” but it should explicitly force Codex to prove equivalence for:

tokens

ordering

API payload meaning

DB behavior

evidence linkage

severity/materiality/risk outputs

narrative outputs

anomaly outputs

2. Before-vs-after artifact comparison
For a refactor phase, Codex should not just rerun tests. It should also compare:

selected deterministic outputs before refactor

same outputs after refactor

and confirm byte-for-byte or semantically exact equivalence

3. Shared-kernel extraction boundaries
The prompt should explicitly say what may be centralized and what must remain local.
Otherwise Codex may over-centralize domain behavior.

4. Backward-compatibility of tokens and version hashes
This is critical.
If shared token builders are centralized but token output changes, you’ve broken the platform historically.

5. Refactor rollback safety
A refactor phase should explicitly require:

easy rollback

no mixed half-migrated abstractions

no dead helper leftovers

no duplicate source of truth after extraction

My recommendation
For Phase 2.1, don’t replace the whole prompt yet.
Add a Refactor Enforcement Addendum to harden it.

Use this exact addendum with Codex.

🔒 PHASE 2.1 — REFACTOR ENFORCEMENT ADDENDUM
This phase is a strict no-drift refactor phase.
In addition to the earlier prompt, the following are mandatory.

A. Exact no-drift equivalence proof
Codex must prove that refactored modules preserve exact prior behavior for representative fixtures across all frozen modules.

At minimum compare before-vs-after outputs for:

normalization run tokens

reconciliation run tokens

ratio/variance run tokens

financial risk run tokens

anomaly run tokens

board pack run tokens

deterministic ordering of results

severity/materiality classifications

confidence classifications

narrative block outputs

evidence link payloads

API response shapes and meanings

If any of these drift, the refactor fails.

B. Artifact snapshot requirement
Before refactor changes, Codex must capture baseline outputs for a representative fixture set from frozen modules.
After refactor, Codex must rerun the same fixtures and compare outputs.

Baseline comparison must include:

token values

run status values

ordered IDs or ordered business keys

computed result payloads

section ordering

narrative texts

board attention ordering

evidence linkage references

C. Shared-kernel extraction limits
Codex may centralize only generic infrastructure patterns.

Allowed to centralize:

token canonicalization helpers

append-only helper builders

supersession validation helpers

dependency graph helpers

common evidence-link helper logic

test harness utilities

migration-head assertion helpers

control-plane registration helpers

Not allowed to centralize if it changes semantics:

ratio formulas

risk scoring rules

anomaly scoring rules

narrative phrasing rules

section inclusion business rules

payroll-specific mapping logic

reconciliation domain classification logic

D. Backward-compatible token guarantee
Any extracted shared token/version helper must preserve exact prior token outputs.

Codex must explicitly verify:

same historical fixture inputs produce identical token strings before and after refactor

If not, refactor fails.

E. Backward-compatible ordering guarantee
Codex must explicitly verify:

same historical fixture inputs produce identical ordered outputs before and after refactor

This includes:

result ordering

section ordering

anomaly ordering

board attention ordering

evidence ordering

F. No hidden semantic merge
Codex must not merge multiple domain-specific rules into one shared abstraction if doing so weakens future module independence.

The refactor must preserve:

module autonomy

domain boundaries

separate freeze-line discipline

G. Dual-source-of-truth prohibition
After extraction, Codex must remove obsolete duplicated helper logic or clearly isolate legacy wrappers.

It must not leave:

old helper and new helper both active

duplicate token logic

duplicate append-only logic

duplicate supersession logic

There must be one authoritative shared implementation where extraction is completed.

H. Rollback safety
Refactor must be organized so it can be reverted cleanly.
No partial migration to new abstractions across only some modules unless wrapped safely.

I. Refactor-specific regression pack
In addition to the full suite, Codex must run a no-drift regression pack that explicitly validates:

token equivalence

output equivalence

ordering equivalence

API equivalence

evidence-link equivalence

J. Final output format addition
Codex must add these sections to its summary:

Shared utilities extracted

Domain logic intentionally left local

Before-vs-after equivalence checks performed

Any known non-functional drift

No-drift verdict: PASS / FAIL

If any non-functional drift exists, do not commit or tag.

For feature phases, broad governance structure is usually enough.
For refactor phases, the dangerous failures are subtle:

token drift

ordering drift

semantic drift

over-centralization

duplicate helpers

broken historical reproducibility

That’s why 2.1 needs stronger wording than 1F.x build phases.

Almost perfect — but one critical correction is needed.

Right now your snippet reads like this:

change business logic
change deterministic outputs
change token values
...
That wording is dangerous.

As written, it reads like you are allowing those changes.

You need to explicitly frame them as FORBIDDEN ACTIONS.

Otherwise Codex may interpret them as change objectives instead of prohibitions.

✅ Correct Safe Version (Use This)
Replace the first block with:

You must NOT:

- change business logic
- change deterministic outputs
- change token values
- change output ordering
- change risk/ratio/anomaly/narrative semantics
- change DB meaning
- change RLS behavior
- change append-only behavior
- widen control-plane permissions
Everything else below that is fine.

Why This Matters
Refactor phases fail because of ambiguous wording.

If the instruction isn’t explicitly negative (“must not”), LLMs sometimes interpret it as scope.

In a feature phase that’s minor.
In a refactor phase it can silently mutate behavior.

We are guarding against:

token drift

ordering drift

semantic drift

enforcement drift

So language precision matters.

Final Verdict
Yes — give the prompt.

But fix that block to:

“You must NOT:”

Then it is safe.

If you want one last layer of paranoia-level safety, I can give you a 3-line “Refactor Kill Switch Clause” to add at the bottom that prevents Codex from committing if equivalence proof is missing.

🔐 CODEX MASTER PROMPT
Phase 2.1 — Architectural Refactoring & Shared Kernel Hardening
Non-Functional, Behavior-Preserving, Regression-Locked Refactor Phase
0. SYSTEM CONTEXT
We are continuing from a platform with the following frozen, DB-verified modules:

Phase 1F.1 — MIS Manager

Phase 1F.2 — Reconciliation Bridge

Phase 1F.3 — Payroll / GL Normalization

Phase 1F.3.1 — Payroll ↔ GL Reconciliation

Phase 1F.4 — Ratio & Variance Engine

Phase 1F.5 — Financial Risk & Materiality Propagation Engine

Phase 1F.6 — Anomaly & Pattern Detection Engine

Phase 1F.7 — Board Pack & Narrative Engine

All these modules are behaviorally frozen.

This phase is not a feature phase.
This phase is not allowed to change business meaning.
This phase is a shared-kernel refactor and hardening phase only.

1. PHASE PURPOSE
The purpose of Phase 2.1 is to:

reduce duplication across frozen modules

extract shared kernel infrastructure

standardize repeated deterministic patterns

consolidate repeated test harness logic

harden shared infrastructure

improve maintainability and architectural clarity

without changing:

deterministic outputs

token values

ordering

API semantics

DB semantics

RLS behavior

append-only behavior

supersession behavior

domain logic meaning

This phase must end with a no-drift proof.

2. FROZEN MODULE PROTECTION BOUNDARY
The following modules are frozen and must remain behaviorally identical before and after refactor:

MIS Manager

Reconciliation Bridge

Payroll / GL Normalization

Payroll ↔ GL Reconciliation

Ratio & Variance Engine

Financial Risk Engine

Anomaly & Pattern Engine

Board Pack & Narrative Engine

change business logic

change deterministic outputs

change token values

change version hash values

change output ordering

change risk semantics

change ratio semantics

change anomaly semantics

change narrative semantics

change DB meaning

change API meaning

change RLS behavior

change FORCE RLS behavior

change append-only behavior

change supersession behavior

change dependency-graph behavior

widen control-plane permissions

weaken control-plane enforcement

introduce new business features

introduce new financial formulas

alter historical reproducibility

If any of the above drift, the phase fails.

5. SHARED KERNEL TARGET AREA
Create or strengthen a shared kernel area such as:

backend/financeops/shared_kernel/

backend/financeops/shared_kernel/
  tokens/
  append_only/
  supersession/
  dependency_graph/
  lineage/
  control_plane/
  validation/
  testing/
  migrations/

You must NOT centralize or merge domain-specific business behavior such as:

materiality semantics

anomaly persistence semantics

If token builders are centralized, the shared implementation must preserve exact existing outputs.

same inputs produce identical token strings before and after refactor

same ordering and canonicalization are preserved

same hash algorithm is preserved

same key ordering and serialization are preserved

same whitespace / null / empty normalization behavior is preserved

If any token changes, the phase fails.

9. ORDERING COMPATIBILITY REQUIREMENT
If deterministic ordering helpers are centralized, the resulting ordering must remain identical.

You must explicitly verify:

same inputs produce the same ordered outputs before and after refactor

no unordered set/dict behavior leaks in

no ORM default ordering drift occurs

no SQL query ordering drift occurs

This applies to:

results

narrative blocks

board attention items

evidence links

ranked outputs

DELETE is still blocked where required

no ORM bypass exists

append-only registry remains complete

No append-only weakening is allowed.

11. SUPERSESSION HARDENING SCOPE
You may centralize supersession validation patterns such as:

duplicate active version checks

12. DEPENDENCY GRAPH HARDENING SCOPE

anomaly correlation/persistence dependencies

You must verify after refactor:

cycle detection remains identical

acyclic validation remains intact

deterministic topological ordering remains identical

no false accepts or false rejects are introduced

13. CONTROL-PLANE HARDENING SCOPE
You may centralize control-plane helper patterns such as:

common enforcement wrapper logic

You must verify after refactor:

18. ENUM / CONSTANT NORMALIZATION

persisted values remain unchanged

Examples may include:

common control-plane constant names

No semantic drift is allowed.

After extracting shared logic, you must eliminate duplicate active implementations.

You must not leave:

two token builders both active

two append-only helpers both active

two migration assertion paths both active

It must not:

📘 CODEX MASTER PROMPT
Phase 2.2 — Performance Optimization Hardening
Non-Functional, Behavior-Preserving, Profiling-Guided Hardening Phase
0️⃣ PHASE CLASSIFICATION
This is a STRICTLY NON-FUNCTIONAL PERFORMANCE PHASE.

It must:

improve or harden performance

reduce latency

reduce DB round-trips

eliminate N+1 patterns

improve query efficiency

validate indexing strategy

reduce redundant computation

optimize deterministic pipelines

It must NOT:

change business logic

change deterministic outputs

change token values

change output ordering

change risk/ratio/anomaly/narrative semantics

change DB meaning

change API meaning

change RLS behavior

change append-only behavior

change supersession behavior

widen control-plane permissions

change domain formulas

alter materiality thresholds

alter severity classifications

Any behavioral drift = hard failure.

1️⃣ SCOPE
Frozen modules in scope:

MIS Manager

Reconciliation Bridge

Payroll / GL Normalization

Payroll ↔ GL Reconciliation

Ratio & Variance Engine

Financial Risk Engine

Anomaly & Pattern Detection Engine

Board Pack & Narrative Engine

Shared Kernel (Phase 2.1)

All are behaviorally locked.

2️⃣ PRIMARY OBJECTIVES
This phase must:

Identify performance bottlenecks using profiling.

Eliminate N+1 database access patterns.

Optimize hot-path query patterns.

Review and add missing indexes (only if safe).

Reduce unnecessary serialization.

Reduce redundant hashing/computation.

Improve deterministic run efficiency.

Improve integration test execution efficiency (without weakening coverage).

Improve API latency where measurable.

Preserve strict deterministic equivalence.

3️⃣ PROFILING REQUIREMENT (MANDATORY FIRST STEP)
Before any optimization:

You must perform profiling on:

Full integration suite

Representative run flows for each engine

Hot deterministic token build paths

Reconciliation flows

Ratio computation flows

Risk propagation flows

Anomaly detection flows

Board pack generation flows

Collect:

DB query counts

DB query time distribution

Python function hotspots

repeated serialization costs

repeated hash costs

repeated JSON parsing costs

redundant sorting costs

N+1 patterns

Produce a profiling summary.

No optimization may be implemented without profiling evidence.

4️⃣ BASELINE CAPTURE (NO-DRIFT CONTROL)
Before optimization:

Capture baseline metrics:

token outputs

ordered outputs

computed values

API response samples

RLS enforcement behavior

append-only enforcement behavior

supersession behavior

dependency validation behavior

Also capture:

execution time metrics

query counts per flow

average latency per API route

These will be used for before–after comparison.

5️⃣ ABSOLUTE PROHIBITIONS
You must NOT:

rewrite business logic

alter formula implementations

alter risk propagation logic

alter anomaly scoring rules

alter narrative semantics

remove validation rules

weaken RLS

weaken append-only

weaken supersession constraints

remove DB constraints

bypass control-plane enforcement

introduce caching that breaks determinism

introduce global mutable state

introduce race conditions

introduce parallelism that breaks ordering

introduce async behavior that changes execution order

introduce non-deterministic ordering

Performance must never override correctness.

6️⃣ N+1 ELIMINATION STRATEGY
You must:

identify N+1 query patterns

consolidate into batched queries

use eager loading where safe

reduce repetitive row-by-row fetches

avoid per-row DB lookups

avoid per-row hash lookups if batchable

All batched optimizations must preserve ordering and result equivalence.

7️⃣ QUERY OPTIMIZATION STRATEGY
You may:

reduce SELECT column scope

add explicit ordering clauses

add missing WHERE clauses

convert suboptimal joins

reduce redundant queries

collapse redundant count queries

reduce repeated identical queries

You must not:

alter logical filtering

remove correctness checks

remove validation logic

weaken transactional integrity

8️⃣ INDEX REVIEW & HARDENING
Perform index audit:

For each frequently queried table:

verify existence of PK index

verify foreign key index

verify frequently filtered column indexes

verify ordering columns indexed

verify join columns indexed

You may add indexes only if:

they do not alter semantic meaning

they do not weaken uniqueness constraints

they do not replace required DB constraints

After adding indexes:

verify fresh migration path

verify no index conflicts

verify no schema drift

9️⃣ HASHING & TOKEN PERFORMANCE HARDENING
Since token hashing is central:

identify repeated canonicalization

reduce duplicate serialization

avoid repeated hashing of identical payloads

avoid re-building identical sorted lists multiple times

But:

token value must remain identical

canonicalization must remain identical

hash algorithm must remain identical

You must explicitly verify token equivalence after optimization.

🔟 DETERMINISTIC PIPELINE HARDENING
For each engine:

verify topological sorting efficiency

verify deterministic ordering preserved

reduce redundant sorting

avoid sorting already sorted lists

avoid repeated stable-sorting on identical data

Ordering must remain identical.

1️⃣1️⃣ SERIALIZATION OPTIMIZATION
Identify:

repeated JSON dumps

repeated JSON loads

repeated dict sorting

repeated canonicalization

Optimize where safe.

Must preserve:

JSON field ordering (if relied upon)

token equivalence

output equivalence

1️⃣2️⃣ MEMORY FOOTPRINT REVIEW
Check:

large in-memory aggregations

unnecessary object duplication

repeated object creation

large intermediate lists

Optimize while preserving determinism.

1️⃣3️⃣ BOARD PACK PERFORMANCE HARDENING
Specifically review:

narrative assembly

section inclusion evaluation

evidence resolution

ordering logic

Ensure:

no additional queries per section

no repeated risk/anomaly recalculation

no repeated DB fetches

Preserve narrative output exactly.

1️⃣4️⃣ RISK & ANOMALY PROPAGATION PERFORMANCE
Review:

propagation graph traversal

repeated dependency traversal

repeated lookups

Optimize graph traversal while preserving:

same dependency ordering

same propagation semantics

same conflict resolution behavior

1️⃣5️⃣ RLS COST REVIEW
Ensure:

RLS policies do not cause excessive repeated scans

required tenant filters are indexed

queries use tenant filter early

Do NOT weaken RLS.

1️⃣6️⃣ APPEND-ONLY PERFORMANCE REVIEW
Ensure:

append-only trigger logic does not introduce redundant overhead

registry lookup is efficient

no unnecessary repeated validation per row

Do NOT remove append-only protection.

1️⃣7️⃣ SUPERSESSION PERFORMANCE REVIEW
Ensure:

supersession validation is not repeatedly recalculating chains unnecessarily

cycle checks are efficient

active version lookup optimized

Preserve semantics exactly.

1️⃣8️⃣ API LATENCY REVIEW
Measure:

route execution time

DB time per route

serialization time

permission-check time

Optimize where safe.

Do NOT remove permission checks.

1️⃣9️⃣ CONTROL-PLANE PERFORMANCE REVIEW
Review:

permission lookup caching

repeated module enablement checks

redundant registry lookups

Optimize safely.

No permission widening allowed.

2️⃣0️⃣ CONCURRENCY SAFETY
Do NOT introduce:

shared mutable global caches

unsafe in-memory memoization

non-tenant-safe caches

cross-request data leakage

race conditions

If caching is introduced:

must be request-scoped

must preserve determinism

must not cross tenant boundaries

2️⃣1️⃣ TEST PERFORMANCE OPTIMIZATION
You may:

optimize DB bootstrap time

optimize fixture reuse safely

optimize test setup overhead

You must NOT:

reduce test coverage

remove invariant tests

bypass heavy validations

reduce migration checks

2️⃣2️⃣ NO-DRIFT EQUIVALENCE CHECKS
After optimization:

You must explicitly verify:

token equivalence

ordering equivalence

output equivalence

API equivalence

RLS equivalence

append-only equivalence

dependency graph equivalence

Provide explicit PASS/FAIL for each.

2️⃣3️⃣ FRESH DB MIGRATION VERIFICATION

verify fresh DB migration

verify alembic head

verify no migration regression

verify constraints preserved

2️⃣4️⃣ FULL REGRESSION SUITE
Must run:

full integration suite

🔐 PHASE 2.3 — MULTI-ENTITY / CONSOLIDATION EXTENSION
Full Audit-Grade Design + Codex Master Prompt
Governance-Locked, 29-Control Architecture
0️⃣ PHASE CLASSIFICATION
This is a NEW CAPABILITY PHASE built on top of an already frozen and hardened deterministic finance platform.

This phase must:

extend the platform from single-entity/scoped intelligence to multi-entity/group-level intelligence

support entity hierarchy modeling

support consolidation-aware aggregation

support intercompany handling hooks

support group-level metrics, risks, anomalies, and board-pack outputs

preserve deterministic, append-only, replay-safe behavior

This phase must NOT:

weaken prior module behavior

mutate upstream outputs

change prior tokens or semantics

create journals automatically

silently net intercompany balances without explicit rules

collapse entity-level lineage

1️⃣ AUDIT-FIRST REQUIREMENT
Before implementation, Codex must perform a design and code audit of the current platform to determine:

current organization/entity/group structures already present

existing tables related to tenant, organisation, group entity, legal entity, business unit, cost center

current RLS patterns that assume single-entity scope

current module assumptions that may block multi-entity extension

current ratio/risk/anomaly/board-pack engines and how they scope organisation_id, tenant_id, source_scope_json, and reporting periods

where entity hierarchy should be linked without breaking prior phases

Codex must return an audit summary first internally in its work, then implement against that reality.

No assumption should override actual repo state.

2️⃣ OBJECTIVE
Implement Phase 2.3 — Multi-Entity / Consolidation Extension as a deterministic extension layer that enables:

entity hierarchy modeling

group-level scope selection

consolidated metric computation

consolidated variance/risk/anomaly outputs

board packs at consolidated/group level

intercompany handling hooks

elimination-adjustment hooks (not auto-posting)

group lineage and drillability

entity-level and group-level coexistence

This must be done without changing the existing meaning of frozen single-entity phases.

1F.1 — MIS Manager

This phase may extend their inputs/consumers, but must not silently alter existing behavior for single-entity execution.

4️⃣ SEPARATE MODULE / EXTENSION BOUNDARY

backend/financeops/modules/multi_entity_consolidation/

Root cause found

Primary blocker (test_tenant_migration_workflow_deterministic_state) was pre-existing environment-sensitive test harness wiring, not a Phase 2.3 domain regression.
The test executed Temporal activities that used global session.py AsyncSessionLocal (from runtime settings.DATABASE_URL) instead of pytest’s local test engine, causing socket.gaierror [Errno 11001] getaddrinfo failed.
Secondary blocker after that fix was expected-version drift in migration tests (they still asserted old head 0019... after adding Phase 2.3 migration).
Phase 2.3 impact determination

Temporal connectivity failure: pre-existing harness dependency exposed during broader suite.
Migration-head assertion failures: caused by introducing new migration head in Phase 2.3, fixed by updating test expectations to new head.

🔐 PHASE 2.4 — FX TRANSLATION & REPORTING CURRENCY LAYER
Full Audit-Grade Design + Codex Master Prompt
Governance-Locked, Deterministic, 29-Control Architecture
0️⃣ PHASE CLASSIFICATION
This is a NEW CAPABILITY PHASE built on top of an already frozen deterministic multi-entity finance platform.

This phase must:

introduce explicit reporting currency support

introduce explicit FX translation rules

introduce deterministic rate selection policies

support translated consolidated outputs

preserve source-currency outputs unchanged

preserve append-only, replay-safe, deterministic behavior

provide drillable rate lineage

This phase must NOT:

silently convert historical outputs in place

mutate source-currency results

auto-post FX journals

apply implicit or guessed FX rates

mix closing/average/historical rates without rule definition

weaken prior month-end locked behavior where relevant upstream

weaken prior no-FX semantics of Phase 2.3 for existing consolidated runs

1️⃣ AUDIT-FIRST REQUIREMENT (MANDATORY)
Before implementation, Codex MUST audit the repository to determine:

what FX/rate structures already exist

what upstream modules already persist FX-related fields

what “month-end locked” or selected-rate services exist in prior accounting phases

how 2.3 consolidation currently stores consolidated outputs and evidence

what reporting currency concepts, if any, already exist

whether current ratio/risk/anomaly/board-pack engines assume source currency only

how existing rate tables/services are accessed and whether they are permissible for reuse

Codex must align design to actual repository state.
No assumption may override code reality.

Implementation may begin only after internal audit alignment.

2️⃣ OBJECTIVE
Implement Phase 2.4 — FX Translation & Reporting Currency Layer as a deterministic extension that enables:

reporting currency definitions

versioned FX translation rules

deterministic rate selection policies

translated consolidated metric / variance / risk / anomaly / board-pack outputs

drillable lineage from translated result → source result → applied rate → rule version

coexistence of source-currency and reporting-currency outputs

Without changing the meaning of prior frozen non-FX outputs.

3️⃣ FROZEN MODULE PROTECTION BOUNDARY
The following frozen modules must remain behaviorally compatible:

1F.1 — MIS Manager

1F.2 — Reconciliation Bridge

1F.3 — Payroll / GL Normalization

1F.3.1 — Payroll ↔ GL Reconciliation

1F.4 — Ratio & Variance Engine

1F.5 — Financial Risk Engine

1F.6 — Anomaly & Pattern Detection Engine

1F.7 — Board Pack & Narrative Engine

2.1 — Shared Kernel Hardening

2.2 — Performance Hardening

2.3 — Multi-Entity / Consolidation Extension

This phase may extend outputs/consumers but must not silently alter existing source-currency or non-FX consolidated behavior.

4️⃣ SEPARATE MODULE / EXTENSION BOUNDARY
Implement as a separate module or isolated extension layer, for example:

backend/financeops/modules/fx_translation_reporting/
Do NOT inject FX translation business logic directly into:

accounting engines

normalization modules

reconciliation bridge core

ratio/risk/anomaly/board-pack engines in a way that breaks source-currency flows

2.3 consolidation core in a way that makes reporting-currency mandatory

Allowed additive touches:

router registration

control-plane permission registration

DB model registration

append-only registry extension

safe additive hooks for translated-output consumption

5️⃣ CORE DESIGN PRINCIPLES
This phase must be:

deterministic

append-only

rate-source aware

rule-version aware

reporting-currency aware

replay-safe

drillable

tenant-isolated

control-plane enforced

backward-compatible

no-posting

no silent fallback

It must preserve:

source-currency outputs

prior run semantics

prior tokens for non-FX runs

prior API meanings unless safely extended

🔟 FX SEMANTIC BOUNDARIES (LOCKED)
Phase 2.4 v1 must explicitly lock the following:

No auto-posting of FX journals.

No silent translation of historical frozen outputs in place.

No implicit averaging if policy requires closing rate.

No implicit closing-rate use if policy requires average/historical rate.

No guessed rates if required rate missing.

No bypass of month-end locked requirement if upstream semantics depend on it.

No silent mix of reporting currencies within one translated run.

No silent restatement of source-currency outputs.

If required rates are missing and policy is fail-closed, the run must fail.
